immediately following the CRLF that concludes the authentication
exchange for the client and the CRLF of the tagged OK response for the
server.[¶](#section-6.2.2-9){.pilcrow}

While client and server implementations [MUST]{.bcp14} implement the
AUTHENTICATE command itself, it is not required to implement any
authentication mechanisms other than the PLAIN mechanism described in
\[[PLAIN](#RFC4616){.xref}\]. Also, an authentication mechanism is not
required to support any security layers.[¶](#section-6.2.2-10){.pilcrow}

Note: a server implementation [MUST]{.bcp14} implement a configuration
in which it does NOT permit any plaintext password mechanisms, unless
the STARTTLS command has been negotiated, TLS has been negotiated on an
Implicit TLS port, or some other mechanism that protects the session
from password snooping has been provided. Server sites [SHOULD
NOT]{.bcp14} use any configuration that permits a plaintext password
mechanism without such a protection mechanism against password snooping.
Client and server implementations [SHOULD]{.bcp14} implement additional
\[[SASL](#RFC4422){.xref}\] mechanisms that do not use plaintext
passwords, such as the GSSAPI mechanism described in
\[[RFC4752](#RFC4752){.xref}\], the SCRAM-SHA-256/SCRAM-SHA-256-PLUS
\[[SCRAM-SHA-256](#RFC7677){.xref}\] mechanisms, and/or the EXTERNAL
\[[SASL](#RFC4422){.xref}\] mechanism for mutual TLS authentication.
(Note that the SASL framework allows for the creation of SASL mechanisms
that support 2-factor authentication (2FA); however, none are fully
ready to be recommended by this
document.)[¶](#section-6.2.2-11){.pilcrow}

Servers and clients can support multiple authentication mechanisms. The
server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} list its supported authentication mechanisms in
the response to the CAPABILITY command so that the client knows which
authentication mechanisms to use.[¶](#section-6.2.2-12){.pilcrow}

A server [MAY]{.bcp14} include a CAPABILITY response code in the tagged
OK response of a successful AUTHENTICATE command in order to send
capabilities automatically. It is unnecessary for a client to send a
separate CAPABILITY command if it recognizes these automatic
capabilities. This should only be done if a security layer was not
negotiated by the AUTHENTICATE command, because the tagged OK response
as part of an AUTHENTICATE command is not protected by
encryption/integrity checking. \[[SASL](#RFC4422){.xref}\] requires the
client to re-issue a CAPABILITY command in this case. The server
[MAY]{.bcp14} advertise different capabilities after a successful
AUTHENTICATE command.[¶](#section-6.2.2-13){.pilcrow}

If an AUTHENTICATE command fails with a NO response, the client
[MAY]{.bcp14} try another authentication mechanism by issuing another
AUTHENTICATE command. It [MAY]{.bcp14} also attempt to authenticate by
using the LOGIN command (see [Section 6.2.3](#login){.xref} for more
detail). In other words, the client [MAY]{.bcp14} request authentication
types in decreasing order of preference, with the LOGIN command as a
last resort.[¶](#section-6.2.2-14){.pilcrow}

The authorization identity passed from the client to the server during
the authentication exchange is interpreted by the server as the user
name whose privileges the client is
requesting.[¶](#section-6.2.2-15){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.2.2-16){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.2.2-17}
``` sourcecode
  S: * OK [CAPABILITY IMAP4rev2 STARTTLS AUTH=GSSAPI]
   Capabilities
  C: A001 AUTHENTICATE GSSAPI
  S: +
  C: YIIB+wYJKoZIhvcSAQICAQBuggHqMIIB5qADAgEFoQMCAQ6iBw
     MFACAAAACjggEmYYIBIjCCAR6gAwIBBaESGxB1Lndhc2hpbmd0
     b24uZWR1oi0wK6ADAgEDoSQwIhsEaW1hcBsac2hpdmFtcy5jYW
     Mud2FzaGluZ3Rvbi5lZHWjgdMwgdCgAwIBAaEDAgEDooHDBIHA
     cS1GSa5b+fXnPZNmXB9SjL8Ollj2SKyb+3S0iXMljen/jNkpJX
     AleKTz6BQPzj8duz8EtoOuNfKgweViyn/9B9bccy1uuAE2HI0y
     C/PHXNNU9ZrBziJ8Lm0tTNc98kUpjXnHZhsMcz5Mx2GR6dGknb
     I0iaGcRerMUsWOuBmKKKRmVMMdR9T3EZdpqsBd7jZCNMWotjhi
     vd5zovQlFqQ2Wjc2+y46vKP/iXxWIuQJuDiisyXF0Y8+5GTpAL
     pHDc1/pIGmMIGjoAMCAQGigZsEgZg2on5mSuxoDHEA1w9bcW9n
     FdFxDKpdrQhVGVRDIzcCMCTzvUboqb5KjY1NJKJsfjRQiBYBdE
     NKfzK+g5DlV8nrw81uOcP8NOQCLR5XkoMHC0Dr/80ziQzbNqhx
     O6652Npft0LQwJvenwDI13YxpwOdMXzkWZN/XrEqOWp6GCgXTB
     vCyLWLlWnbaUkZdEYbKHBPjd8t/1x5Yg==
  S: + YGgGCSqGSIb3EgECAgIAb1kwV6ADAgEFoQMCAQ+iSzBJoAMC
     AQGiQgRAtHTEuOP2BXb9sBYFR4SJlDZxmg39IxmRBOhXRKdDA0
     uHTCOT9Bq3OsUTXUlk0CsFLoa8j+gvGDlgHuqzWHPSQg==
  C:
  S: + YDMGCSqGSIb3EgECAgIBAAD/////6jcyG4GE3KkTzBeBiVHe
     ceP2CWY0SR0fAQAgAAQEBAQ=
  C: YDMGCSqGSIb3EgECAgIBAAD/////3LQBHXTpFfZgrejpLlLImP
     wkhbfa2QteAQAgAG1yYwE=
  S: A001 OK GSSAPI authentication successful
```

[¶](#section-6.2.2-17){.pilcrow}
:::

The following example demonstrates the use of an initial
response.[¶](#section-6.2.2-18){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.2.2-19){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.2.2-20}
``` sourcecode
  S: * OK [CAPABILITY IMAP4rev2 STARTTLS AUTH=GSSAPI
   LOGINDISABLED] Server ready
  C: A01 STARTTLS
  S: A01 OK STARTTLS completed
  <TLS negotiation, further commands are under TLS layer>
  C: A02 CAPABILITY
  S: * CAPABILITY IMAP4rev2 AUTH=GSSAPI AUTH=PLAIN
  S: A02 OK CAPABILITY completed
  C: A03 AUTHENTICATE PLAIN dGVzdAB0ZXN0AHRlc3Q=
  S: A03 OK Success (tls protection)
```

[¶](#section-6.2.2-20){.pilcrow}
:::

Note that because the initial response is optional, the following
negotiation (which does not use the initial response) is still valid and
[MUST]{.bcp14} be supported by the
server:[¶](#section-6.2.2-21){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.2.2-22}
``` sourcecode
  ... client connects to server and negotiates a TLS
      protection layer ...
  C: C01 CAPABILITY
  S: * CAPABILITY IMAP4rev2 AUTH=PLAIN
  S: C01 OK Completed
  C: A01 AUTHENTICATE PLAIN
  S: +
  C: dGVzdAB0ZXN0AHRlc3Q=
  S: A01 OK Success (tls protection)
```

[¶](#section-6.2.2-22){.pilcrow}
:::

Note that in the above example there is a space following the \"+\" from
the server.[¶](#section-6.2.2-23){.pilcrow}

The following is an example authentication using the SASL EXTERNAL
mechanism (defined in \[[SASL](#RFC4422){.xref}\]) under a TLS
protection layer and an empty initial
response:[¶](#section-6.2.2-24){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.2.2-25}
``` sourcecode
  ... client connects to server and negotiates a TLS
      protection layer ...
  C: C01 CAPABILITY
  S: * CAPABILITY IMAP4rev2 AUTH=PLAIN AUTH=EXTERNAL
  S: C01 OK Completed
  C: A01 AUTHENTICATE EXTERNAL =
  S: A01 OK Success (tls protection)
```

[¶](#section-6.2.2-25){.pilcrow}
:::

Note: The line breaks within server challenges and client responses are
for editorial clarity and are not in real
authenticators.[¶](#section-6.2.2-26){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#login}
::: {#section-6.2.3 .section}
#### [6.2.3.](#section-6.2.3){.section-number .selfRef} [LOGIN Command](#name-login-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-login-command}

[]{.break}

Arguments:

:   user name[¶](#section-6.2.3-1.2.1){.pilcrow}

    password[¶](#section-6.2.3-1.2.2){.pilcrow}

:   

Responses:
:   no specific responses for this
    command[¶](#section-6.2.3-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   login completed, now in authenticated
        state[¶](#section-6.2.3-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   login failure: user name or password
        rejected[¶](#section-6.2.3-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.2.3-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The LOGIN command identifies the client to the server and carries the
plaintext password authenticating this user. The LOGIN command [SHOULD
NOT]{.bcp14} be used except as a last resort (after attempting and
failing to authenticate using the AUTHENTICATE command one or more
times), and it is recommended that client implementations have a means
to disable any automatic use of the LOGIN
command.[¶](#section-6.2.3-2){.pilcrow}

A server [MAY]{.bcp14} include a CAPABILITY response code in the tagged
OK response to a successful LOGIN command in order to send capabilities
automatically. It is unnecessary for a client to send a separate
CAPABILITY command if it recognizes these automatic
capabilities.[¶](#section-6.2.3-3){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.2.3-4){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.2.3-5}
``` sourcecode
  C: a001 LOGIN SMITH SESAME
  S: a001 OK LOGIN completed
```

[¶](#section-6.2.3-5){.pilcrow}
:::

Note: Use of the LOGIN command over an insecure network (such as the
Internet) is a security risk, because anyone monitoring network traffic
can obtain plaintext passwords. For that reason, clients [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} use LOGIN on unsecure
networks.[¶](#section-6.2.3-6){.pilcrow}

Unless the client is accessing IMAP service on an Implicit TLS port
\[[RFC8314](#RFC8314){.xref}\], the STARTTLS command has been
negotiated, or some other mechanism that protects the session from
password snooping has been provided, a server implementation
[MUST]{.bcp14} implement a configuration in which it advertises the
LOGINDISABLED capability and does NOT permit the LOGIN command. Server
sites [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14} use any configuration that permits the LOGIN
command without such a protection mechanism against password snooping. A
client implementation [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} send a LOGIN command if the
LOGINDISABLED capability is advertised.[¶](#section-6.2.3-7){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.3 .section}
### [6.3.](#section-6.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Client Commands - Authenticated State](#name-client-commands-authenticat){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-client-commands-authenticat}

In the authenticated state, commands that manipulate mailboxes as atomic
entities are permitted. Of these commands, SELECT and EXAMINE will
select a mailbox for access and enter the selected
state.[¶](#section-6.3-1){.pilcrow}

In addition to the universal commands (CAPABILITY, NOOP, and LOGOUT),
the following commands are valid in the authenticated state: ENABLE,
SELECT, EXAMINE, NAMESPACE, CREATE, DELETE, RENAME, SUBSCRIBE,
UNSUBSCRIBE, LIST, STATUS, APPEND, and
IDLE.[¶](#section-6.3-2){.pilcrow}

::: {#enable-command}
::: {#section-6.3.1 .section}
#### [6.3.1.](#section-6.3.1){.section-number .selfRef} [ENABLE Command](#name-enable-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-enable-command}

[]{#iref-enable-command-39 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   capability names[¶](#section-6.3.1-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   no specific responses for this
    command[¶](#section-6.3.1-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   Relevant capabilities
        enabled[¶](#section-6.3.1-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   No arguments, or syntax error in an
        argument[¶](#section-6.3.1-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Several IMAP extensions allow the server to return unsolicited responses
specific to these extensions in certain circumstances. However, servers
cannot send those unsolicited responses (with the exception of response
codes (see [Section 7.1](#server-status-responses){.xref}) included in
tagged or untagged OK/NO/BAD responses, which can always be sent) until
they know that the clients support such extensions and thus will be able
to correctly parse and process the extension response
data.[¶](#section-6.3.1-2){.pilcrow}

The ENABLE command provides an explicit indication from the client that
it supports particular extensions. It is designed such that the client
can send a simple constant string with the extensions it supports, and
the server will enable the shared subset that both
support.[¶](#section-6.3.1-3){.pilcrow}

The ENABLE command takes a list of capability names and requests the
server to enable the named extensions. Once enabled using ENABLE, each
extension remains active until the IMAP connection is closed. For each
argument, the server does the following:[¶](#section-6.3.1-4){.pilcrow}

-   [If the argument is not an extension known to the server, the server
    [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore the
    argument.[¶](#section-6.3.1-5.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.1-5.1}
-   [If the argument is an extension known to the server, and it is not
    specifically permitted to be enabled using ENABLE, the server
    [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore the argument. (Note that knowing about an
    extension doesn\'t necessarily imply supporting that
    extension.)[¶](#section-6.3.1-5.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.1-5.2}
-   [If the argument is an extension that is supported by the server and
    that needs to be enabled, the server [MUST]{.bcp14} enable the
    extension for the duration of the connection. Note that once an
    extension is enabled, there is no way to disable
    it.[¶](#section-6.3.1-5.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.1-5.3}

If the ENABLE command is successful, the server [MUST]{.bcp14} send an
untagged ENABLED response ([Section 7.2.1](#enabled){.xref}), which
includes all enabled extensions as specified above. The ENABLED response
is sent even if no extensions were
enabled.[¶](#section-6.3.1-6){.pilcrow}

Clients [SHOULD]{.bcp14} only include extensions that need to be enabled
by the server. For example, a client can enable IMAP4rev2-specific
behavior when both IMAP4rev1 and IMAP4rev2 are advertised in the
CAPABILITY response. Future RFCs may add to this
list.[¶](#section-6.3.1-7){.pilcrow}

The ENABLE command is only valid in the authenticated state, before any
mailbox is selected. Clients [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} issue ENABLE once they
SELECT/EXAMINE a mailbox; however, server implementations don\'t have to
check that no mailbox is selected or was previously selected during the
duration of a connection.[¶](#section-6.3.1-8){.pilcrow}

The ENABLE command can be issued multiple times in a session. It is
additive; that is, \"ENABLE a b\", followed by \"ENABLE c\", is the same
as a single command \"ENABLE a b c\". When multiple ENABLE commands are
issued, each corresponding ENABLED response [SHOULD]{.bcp14} only
contain extensions enabled by the corresponding ENABLE command, i.e.,
for the above example, the ENABLED response to \"ENABLE c\" should not
contain \"a\" or \"b\".[¶](#section-6.3.1-9){.pilcrow}

There are no limitations on pipelining ENABLE. For example, it is
possible to send ENABLE and then immediately SELECT, or a LOGIN
immediately followed by ENABLE.[¶](#section-6.3.1-10){.pilcrow}

The server [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} change the CAPABILITY list as a result of
executing ENABLE; that is, a CAPABILITY command issued right after an
ENABLE command [MUST]{.bcp14} list the same capabilities as a CAPABILITY
command issued before the ENABLE command. This is demonstrated in the
following example. Note that below \"X-GOOD-IDEA\" is a fictitious
extension capability that can be
ENABLED.[¶](#section-6.3.1-11){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.1-12}
``` sourcecode
  C: t1 CAPABILITY
  S: * CAPABILITY IMAP4rev2 ID LITERAL+ X-GOOD-IDEA
  S: t1 OK foo
  C: t2 ENABLE CONDSTORE X-GOOD-IDEA
  S: * ENABLED X-GOOD-IDEA
  S: t2 OK foo
  C: t3 CAPABILITY
  S: * CAPABILITY IMAP4rev2 ID LITERAL+ X-GOOD-IDEA
  S: t3 OK foo again
```

[¶](#section-6.3.1-12){.pilcrow}
:::

In the following example, the client enables the Conditional Store
(CONDSTORE) extension
\[[RFC7162](#RFC7162){.xref}\]:[¶](#section-6.3.1-13){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.1-14}
``` sourcecode
  C: a1 ENABLE CONDSTORE
  S: * ENABLED CONDSTORE
  S: a1 OK Conditional Store enabled
```

[¶](#section-6.3.1-14){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.3.1.1 .section}
##### [6.3.1.1.](#section-6.3.1.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Note to Designers of Extensions That May Use the ENABLE Command](#name-note-to-designers-of-extens){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-note-to-designers-of-extens}

Designers of IMAP extensions are discouraged from creating extensions
that require ENABLE unless there is no good alternative design.
Specifically, extensions that cause potentially incompatible behavior
changes to deployed server responses (and thus benefit from ENABLE) have
a higher complexity cost than extensions that do
not.[¶](#section-6.3.1.1-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.3.2 .section}
#### [6.3.2.](#section-6.3.2){.section-number .selfRef} [SELECT Command](#name-select-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-select-command}

[]{#iref-select-command-40 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   mailbox name[¶](#section-6.3.2-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    [REQUIRED]{.bcp14} untagged responses:
    :   FLAGS, EXISTS, LIST[¶](#section-6.3.2-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    [REQUIRED]{.bcp14} OK untagged responses:
    :   PERMANENTFLAGS, UIDNEXT,
        UIDVALIDITY[¶](#section-6.3.2-1.4.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   select completed, now in selected
        state[¶](#section-6.3.2-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   select failure, now in authenticated state: no such mailbox,
        can\'t access mailbox[¶](#section-6.3.2-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.2-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The SELECT command selects a mailbox so that messages in the mailbox can
be accessed. Before returning an OK to the client, the server
[MUST]{.bcp14} send the following untagged data to the client. (The
order of individual responses is not important.) Note that earlier
versions of this protocol, such as the IMAP4rev1 version specified in
\[[RFC2060](#RFC2060){.xref}\], only required the FLAGS and EXISTS
untagged responses and UIDVALIDITY response code. Client implementations
that need to remain compatible with such older IMAP versions have to
implement default behavior for missing data, as discussed with the
individual items.[¶](#section-6.3.2-2){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

FLAGS
:   Defined flags in the mailbox. See the description of the FLAGS
    response in [Section 7.3.5](#flags-resp){.xref} for more
    detail.[¶](#section-6.3.2-3.2){.pilcrow}
:   

\<n> EXISTS
:   The number of messages in the mailbox. See the description of the
    EXISTS response in [Section 7.4.1](#exists){.xref} for more
    detail.[¶](#section-6.3.2-3.4){.pilcrow}
:   

LIST
:   The server [MUST]{.bcp14} return a LIST response with the mailbox
    name. The list of mailbox attributes [MUST]{.bcp14} be accurate. If
    the server allows denormalized UTF-8 mailbox names (see [Section
    5.1](#mailbox-naming){.xref}) and the supplied mailbox name differs
    from the normalized version, the server [MUST]{.bcp14} return LIST
    with the OLDNAME extended data item. See [Section
    6.3.9.7](#oldname){.xref} for more
    details.[¶](#section-6.3.2-3.6){.pilcrow}
:   

OK \[PERMANENTFLAGS (\<list of flags>)\]
:   A list of message flags that the client can change permanently. If
    this is missing, the client should assume that all flags can be
    changed permanently.[¶](#section-6.3.2-3.8){.pilcrow}
:   

OK \[UIDNEXT \<n>\]
:   The next unique identifier value. Refer to [Section
    2.3.1.1](#uid-def){.xref} for more
    information.[¶](#section-6.3.2-3.10){.pilcrow}
:   

OK \[UIDVALIDITY \<n>\]
:   The unique identifier validity value. Refer to [Section
    2.3.1.1](#uid-def){.xref} for more
    information.[¶](#section-6.3.2-3.12){.pilcrow}
:   

Only one mailbox can be selected at a time in a connection; simultaneous
access to multiple mailboxes requires multiple connections. The SELECT
command automatically deselects any currently selected mailbox before
attempting the new selection. Consequently, if a mailbox is selected and
a SELECT command that fails is attempted, no mailbox is selected. When
deselecting a selected mailbox, the server [MUST]{.bcp14} return an
untagged OK response with the \"\[CLOSED\]\" response code when the
currently selected mailbox is closed (see [Section
7.1](#closed){.xref}).[¶](#section-6.3.2-4){.pilcrow}

If the client is permitted to modify the mailbox, the server
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} prefix the text of the tagged OK response with the
\"\[READ-WRITE\]\" response code.[¶](#section-6.3.2-5){.pilcrow}

If the client is not permitted to modify the mailbox but is permitted
read access, the mailbox is selected as read-only, and the server
[MUST]{.bcp14} prefix the text of the tagged OK response to SELECT with
the \"\[READ-ONLY\]\" response code. Read-only access through SELECT
differs from the EXAMINE command in that certain read-only mailboxes
[MAY]{.bcp14} permit the change of permanent state on a per-user (as
opposed to global) basis. Netnews messages marked in a server-based
.newsrc file are an example of such per-user permanent state that can be
modified with read-only mailboxes.[¶](#section-6.3.2-6){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.2-7){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.2-8}
``` sourcecode
  C: A142 SELECT INBOX
  S: * 172 EXISTS
  S: * OK [UIDVALIDITY 3857529045] UIDs valid
  S: * OK [UIDNEXT 4392] Predicted next UID
  S: * FLAGS (\Answered \Flagged \Deleted \Seen \Draft)
  S: * OK [PERMANENTFLAGS (\Deleted \Seen \*)] Limited
  S: * LIST () "/" INBOX
  S: A142 OK [READ-WRITE] SELECT completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.2-8){.pilcrow}
:::

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.2-9){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.2-10}
``` sourcecode
  C: A142 SELECT INBOX
  S: * 172 EXISTS
  S: * OK [UIDVALIDITY 3857529045] UIDs valid
  S: * OK [UIDNEXT 4392] Predicted next UID
  S: * FLAGS (\Answered \Flagged \Deleted \Seen \Draft)
  S: * OK [PERMANENTFLAGS (\Deleted \Seen \*)] Limited
  S: A142 OK [READ-WRITE] SELECT completed
  [...some time later...]
  C: A143 SELECT Drafts
  S: * OK [CLOSED] Previous mailbox is now closed
  S: * 5 EXISTS
  S: * OK [UIDVALIDITY 9877410381] UIDs valid
  S: * OK [UIDNEXT 102] Predicted next UID
  S: * LIST () "/" Drafts
  S: * FLAGS (\Answered \Flagged \Deleted \Seen \Draft)
  S: * OK [PERMANENTFLAGS (\Deleted \Seen \Answered
      \Flagged \Draft \*)] System flags and keywords allowed
  S: A143 OK [READ-WRITE] SELECT completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.2-10){.pilcrow}
:::

Note that IMAP4rev1-compliant servers can also send the untagged RECENT
response that was deprecated in IMAP4rev2, e.g., \"\* 0 RECENT\". Pure
IMAP4rev2 clients are advised to ignore the untagged RECENT
response.[¶](#section-6.3.2-11){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.3.3 .section}
#### [6.3.3.](#section-6.3.3){.section-number .selfRef} [EXAMINE Command](#name-examine-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-examine-command}

[]{#iref-examine-command-41 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   mailbox name[¶](#section-6.3.3-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    [REQUIRED]{.bcp14} untagged responses:
    :   FLAGS, EXISTS, LIST[¶](#section-6.3.3-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    [REQUIRED]{.bcp14} OK untagged responses:
    :   PERMANENTFLAGS, UIDNEXT,
        UIDVALIDITY[¶](#section-6.3.3-1.4.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   examine completed, now in selected
        state[¶](#section-6.3.3-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   examine failure, now in authenticated state: no such mailbox,
        can\'t access mailbox[¶](#section-6.3.3-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.3-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The EXAMINE command is identical to SELECT and returns the same output;
however, the selected mailbox is identified as read-only. No changes to
the permanent state of the mailbox, including per-user state, are
permitted.[¶](#section-6.3.3-2){.pilcrow}

The text of the tagged OK response to the EXAMINE command [MUST]{.bcp14}
begin with the \"\[READ-ONLY\]\" response
code.[¶](#section-6.3.3-3){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.3-4){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.3-5}
``` sourcecode
   C: A932 EXAMINE blurdybloop
   S: * 17 EXISTS
   S: * OK [UIDVALIDITY 3857529045] UIDs valid
   S: * OK [UIDNEXT 4392] Predicted next UID
   S: * LIST () "/" blurdybloop
   S: * FLAGS (\Answered \Flagged \Deleted \Seen \Draft)
   S: * OK [PERMANENTFLAGS ()] No permanent flags permitted
   S: A932 OK [READ-ONLY] EXAMINE completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.3-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.3.4 .section}
#### [6.3.4.](#section-6.3.4){.section-number .selfRef} [CREATE Command](#name-create-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-create-command}

[]{#iref-create-command-42 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   mailbox name[¶](#section-6.3.4-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} untagged response:
    :   LIST[¶](#section-6.3.4-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   create completed[¶](#section-6.3.4-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   create failure: can\'t create mailbox with that
        name[¶](#section-6.3.4-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.4-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The CREATE command creates a mailbox with the given name. An OK response
is returned only if a new mailbox with that name has been created. It is
an error to attempt to create INBOX or a mailbox with a name that refers
to an extant mailbox. Any error in creation will return a tagged NO
response. If a client attempts to create a UTF-8 mailbox name that is
not a valid Net-Unicode name, the server [MUST]{.bcp14} reject the
creation or convert the name to Net-Unicode prior to creating the
mailbox. If the server decides to convert (normalize) the name, it
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} return an untagged LIST with an OLDNAME extended data
item, with the OLDNAME value being the supplied mailbox name and the
name parameter being the normalized mailbox name. (See [Section
6.3.9.7](#oldname){.xref} for more
details.)[¶](#section-6.3.4-2){.pilcrow}

Mailboxes created in one IMAP session [MAY]{.bcp14} be announced to
other IMAP sessions using an unsolicited LIST response. If the server
automatically subscribes a mailbox when it is created, then the
unsolicited LIST response for each affected subscribed mailbox name
[MUST]{.bcp14} include the \\Subscribed
attribute.[¶](#section-6.3.4-3){.pilcrow}

If the mailbox name is suffixed with the server\'s hierarchy separator
character (as returned from the server by a LIST command), this is a
declaration that the client intends to create mailbox names under this
name in the hierarchy. Server implementations that do not require this
declaration [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore the declaration. In any case, the name
created is without the trailing hierarchy
delimiter.[¶](#section-6.3.4-4){.pilcrow}

If the server\'s hierarchy separator character appears elsewhere in the
name, the server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} create any superior hierarchical names
that are needed for the CREATE command to be successfully completed. In
other words, an attempt to create \"foo/bar/zap\" on a server in which
\"/\" is the hierarchy separator character [SHOULD]{.bcp14} create foo/
and foo/bar/ if they do not already
exist.[¶](#section-6.3.4-5){.pilcrow}

If a new mailbox is created with the same name as a mailbox that was
deleted, its unique identifiers [MUST]{.bcp14} be greater than any
unique identifiers used in the previous incarnation of the mailbox
unless the new incarnation has a different unique identifier validity
value. See the description of the UID command in [Section
6.4.9](#uid-commands){.xref} for more
detail.[¶](#section-6.3.4-6){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.4-7){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.4-8}
``` sourcecode
  C: A003 CREATE owatagusiam/
  S: A003 OK CREATE completed
  C: A004 CREATE owatagusiam/blurdybloop
  S: A004 OK CREATE completed
  C: A005 CREATE NonNormalized
  S: * LIST () "/" "Normalized" ("OLDNAME" ("NonNormalized"))
  S: A005 OK CREATE completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.4-8){.pilcrow}
:::

(In the last example, imagine that \"NonNormalized\" is a non-NFC
normalized Unicode mailbox name and that \"Normalized\" is its NFC
normalized version.)[¶](#section-6.3.4-9){.pilcrow}

Note: The interpretation of this example depends on whether \"/\" was
returned as the hierarchy separator from LIST. If \"/\" is the hierarchy
separator, a new level of hierarchy named \"owatagusiam\" with a member
called \"blurdybloop\" is created. Otherwise, two mailboxes at the same
hierarchy level are created.[¶](#section-6.3.4-10.1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.3.5 .section}
#### [6.3.5.](#section-6.3.5){.section-number .selfRef} [DELETE Command](#name-delete-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-delete-command}

[]{#iref-delete-command-43 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   mailbox name[¶](#section-6.3.5-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} untagged response:
    :   LIST[¶](#section-6.3.5-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   delete completed[¶](#section-6.3.5-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   delete failure: can\'t delete mailbox with that
        name[¶](#section-6.3.5-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.5-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The DELETE command permanently removes the mailbox with the given name.
A tagged OK response is returned only if the mailbox has been deleted.
It is an error to attempt to delete INBOX or a mailbox name that does
not exist.[¶](#section-6.3.5-2){.pilcrow}

The DELETE command [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} remove inferior hierarchical
names. For example, if a mailbox \"foo\" has an inferior \"foo.bar\"
(assuming \".\" is the hierarchy delimiter character), removing \"foo\"
[MUST NOT]{.bcp14} remove \"foo.bar\". It is an error to attempt to
delete a name that has inferior hierarchical names and also has the
\\Noselect mailbox name attribute (see the description of the LIST
response ([Section 7.3.1](#list-resp){.xref}) for more
details).[¶](#section-6.3.5-3){.pilcrow}

It is permitted to delete a name that has inferior hierarchical names
and does not have the \\Noselect mailbox name attribute. If the server
implementation does not permit deleting the name while inferior
hierarchical names exist, then it [SHOULD]{.bcp14} disallow the DELETE
command by returning a tagged NO response. The NO response
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} include the HASCHILDREN response code. Alternatively,
the server [MAY]{.bcp14} allow the DELETE command, but it sets the
\\Noselect mailbox name attribute for that
name.[¶](#section-6.3.5-4){.pilcrow}

If the server returns an OK response, all messages in that mailbox are
removed by the DELETE command.[¶](#section-6.3.5-5){.pilcrow}

The value of the highest-used unique identifier of the deleted mailbox
[MUST]{.bcp14} be preserved so that a new mailbox created with the same
name will not reuse the identifiers of the former incarnation, unless
the new incarnation has a different unique identifier validity value.
See the description of the UID command in [Section
6.4.9](#uid-commands){.xref} for more
detail.[¶](#section-6.3.5-6){.pilcrow}

If the server decides to convert (normalize) the mailbox name, it
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} return an untagged LIST with the \"\\NonExistent\"
attribute and OLDNAME extended data item, with the OLDNAME value being
the supplied mailbox name and the name parameter being the normalized
mailbox name. (See [Section 6.3.9.7](#oldname){.xref} for more
details.)[¶](#section-6.3.5-7){.pilcrow}

Mailboxes deleted in one IMAP session [MAY]{.bcp14} be announced to
other IMAP sessions using an unsolicited LIST response, containing the
\"\\NonExistent\" attribute.[¶](#section-6.3.5-8){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.5-9){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.5-10}
``` sourcecode
  C: A682 LIST "" *
  S: * LIST () "/" blurdybloop
  S: * LIST (\Noselect) "/" foo
  S: * LIST () "/" foo/bar
  S: A682 OK LIST completed
  C: A683 DELETE blurdybloop
  S: A683 OK DELETE completed
  C: A684 DELETE foo
  S: A684 NO Name "foo" has inferior hierarchical names
  C: A685 DELETE foo/bar
  S: A685 OK DELETE Completed
  C: A686 LIST "" *
  S: * LIST (\Noselect) "/" foo
  S: A686 OK LIST completed
  C: A687 DELETE foo
  S: A687 OK DELETE Completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.5-10){.pilcrow}
:::

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.5-11){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.5-12}
``` sourcecode
  C: A82 LIST "" *
  S: * LIST () "." blurdybloop
  S: * LIST () "." foo
  S: * LIST () "." foo.bar
  S: A82 OK LIST completed
  C: A83 DELETE blurdybloop
  S: A83 OK DELETE completed
  C: A84 DELETE foo
  S: A84 OK DELETE Completed
  C: A85 LIST "" *
  S: * LIST () "." foo.bar
  S: A85 OK LIST completed
  C: A86 LIST "" %
  S: * LIST (\Noselect) "." foo
  S: A86 OK LIST completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.5-12){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.3.6 .section}
#### [6.3.6.](#section-6.3.6){.section-number .selfRef} [RENAME Command](#name-rename-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-rename-command}

[]{#iref-rename-command-44 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:

:   existing mailbox name[¶](#section-6.3.6-1.2.1){.pilcrow}

    new mailbox name[¶](#section-6.3.6-1.2.2){.pilcrow}

:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} untagged response:
    :   LIST[¶](#section-6.3.6-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   rename completed[¶](#section-6.3.6-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   rename failure: can\'t rename mailbox with that name, can\'t
        rename to mailbox with that
        name[¶](#section-6.3.6-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.6-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The RENAME command changes the name of a mailbox. A tagged OK response
is returned only if the mailbox has been renamed. It is an error to
attempt to rename from a mailbox name that does not exist or to a
mailbox name that already exists. Any error in renaming will return a
tagged NO response.[¶](#section-6.3.6-2){.pilcrow}

If the name has inferior hierarchical names, then the inferior
hierarchical names [MUST]{.bcp14} also be renamed. For example, a rename
of \"foo\" to \"zap\" will rename \"foo/bar\" (assuming \"/\" is the
hierarchy delimiter character) to
\"zap/bar\".[¶](#section-6.3.6-3){.pilcrow}

If the server\'s hierarchy separator character appears in the new
mailbox name, the server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} create any superior
hierarchical names that are needed for the RENAME command to complete
successfully. In other words, an attempt to rename \"foo/bar/zap\" to
\"baz/rag/zowie\" on a server in which \"/\" is the hierarchy separator
character in the corresponding namespace [SHOULD]{.bcp14} create
\"baz/\" and \"baz/rag/\" if they do not already
exist.[¶](#section-6.3.6-4){.pilcrow}

The value of the highest-used unique identifier of the old mailbox name
[MUST]{.bcp14} be preserved so that a new mailbox created with the same
name will not reuse the identifiers of the former incarnation, unless
the new incarnation has a different unique identifier validity value.
See the description of the UID command in [Section
6.4.9](#uid-commands){.xref} for more
detail.[¶](#section-6.3.6-5){.pilcrow}

Renaming INBOX is permitted and does not result in a tagged BAD
response, and it has special behavior: It moves all messages in INBOX to
a new mailbox with the given name, leaving INBOX empty. If the server
implementation supports inferior hierarchical names of INBOX, these are
unaffected by a rename of INBOX. (Note that some servers disallow
renaming INBOX by returning a tagged NO response, so clients need to be
able to handle the failure of such RENAME
commands.)[¶](#section-6.3.6-6){.pilcrow}

If the server allows creation of mailboxes with names that are not valid
Net-Unicode names, the server normalizes both the existing mailbox name
parameter and the new mailbox name parameter. If the normalized version
of any of these 2 parameters differs from the corresponding supplied
version, the server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} return an untagged LIST response
with an OLDNAME extended data item, with the OLDNAME value being the
supplied existing mailbox name and the name parameter being the
normalized new mailbox name (see [Section 6.3.9.7](#oldname){.xref}).
This would allow the client to correlate the supplied name with the
normalized name.[¶](#section-6.3.6-7){.pilcrow}

Mailboxes renamed in one IMAP session [MAY]{.bcp14} be announced to
other IMAP sessions using an unsolicited LIST response with an OLDNAME
extended data item.[¶](#section-6.3.6-8){.pilcrow}

In both of the above cases, if the server automatically subscribes a
mailbox when it is renamed, then the unsolicited LIST response for each
affected subscribed mailbox name [MUST]{.bcp14} include the \\Subscribed
attribute. No unsolicited LIST responses need to be sent for child
mailboxes. When INBOX is successfully renamed, it is assumed that a new
INBOX is created. No unsolicited LIST responses need to be sent for
INBOX in this case.[¶](#section-6.3.6-9){.pilcrow}

Examples:[¶](#section-6.3.6-10){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.6-11}
``` sourcecode
  C: A682 LIST "" *
  S: * LIST () "/" blurdybloop
  S: * LIST (\Noselect) "/" foo
  S: * LIST () "/" foo/bar
  S: A682 OK LIST completed
  C: A683 RENAME blurdybloop sarasoop
  S: A683 OK RENAME completed
  C: A684 RENAME foo zowie
  S: A684 OK RENAME Completed
  C: A685 LIST "" *
  S: * LIST () "/" sarasoop
  S: * LIST (\Noselect) "/" zowie
  S: * LIST () "/" zowie/bar
  S: A685 OK LIST completed

  C: Z432 LIST "" *
  S: * LIST () "." INBOX
  S: * LIST () "." INBOX.bar
  S: Z432 OK LIST completed
  C: Z433 RENAME INBOX old-mail
  S: Z433 OK RENAME completed
  C: Z434 LIST "" *
  S: * LIST () "." INBOX
  S: * LIST () "." INBOX.bar
  S: * LIST () "." old-mail
  S: Z434 OK LIST completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.6-11){.pilcrow}
:::

Note that renaming a mailbox doesn\'t update subscription information on
the original name. To keep subscription information in sync, the
following sequence of commands can be
used:[¶](#section-6.3.6-12){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.6-13}
``` sourcecode
  C: 1001 RENAME X Y
  C: 1002 SUBSCRIBE Y
  C: 1003 UNSUBSCRIBE X
```

[¶](#section-6.3.6-13){.pilcrow}
:::

Note that the above sequence of commands doesn\'t account for updating
the subscription for any child mailboxes of mailbox
X.[¶](#section-6.3.6-14){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.3.7 .section}
#### [6.3.7.](#section-6.3.7){.section-number .selfRef} [SUBSCRIBE Command](#name-subscribe-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-subscribe-command}

[]{#iref-subscribe-command-45 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   mailbox[¶](#section-6.3.7-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   no specific responses for this
    command[¶](#section-6.3.7-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   subscribe completed[¶](#section-6.3.7-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   subscribe failure: can\'t subscribe to that
        name[¶](#section-6.3.7-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.7-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The SUBSCRIBE command adds the specified mailbox name to the server\'s
set of \"active\" or \"subscribed\" mailboxes as returned by the LIST
(SUBSCRIBED) command. This command returns a tagged OK response if the
subscription is successful or if the mailbox is already
subscribed.[¶](#section-6.3.7-2){.pilcrow}

A server [MAY]{.bcp14} validate the mailbox argument to SUBSCRIBE to
verify that it exists. However, it [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14} unilaterally
remove an existing mailbox name from the subscription list even if a
mailbox by that name no longer exists.[¶](#section-6.3.7-3){.pilcrow}

Note: This requirement is because a server site can choose to routinely
remove a mailbox with a well-known name (e.g., \"system-alerts\") after
its contents expire, with the intention of recreating it when new
contents are appropriate.[¶](#section-6.3.7-4.1){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.7-5){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.7-6}
``` sourcecode
  C: A002 SUBSCRIBE #news.comp.mail.mime
  S: A002 OK SUBSCRIBE completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.7-6){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.3.8 .section}
#### [6.3.8.](#section-6.3.8){.section-number .selfRef} [UNSUBSCRIBE Command](#name-unsubscribe-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-unsubscribe-command}

[]{#iref-unsubscribe-command-46 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   mailbox name[¶](#section-6.3.8-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   no specific responses for this
    command[¶](#section-6.3.8-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   unsubscribe completed[¶](#section-6.3.8-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   unsubscribe failure: can\'t unsubscribe that
        name[¶](#section-6.3.8-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.8-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The UNSUBSCRIBE command removes the specified mailbox name from the
server\'s set of \"active\" or \"subscribed\" mailboxes as returned by
the LIST (SUBSCRIBED) command. This command returns a tagged OK response
if the unsubscription is successful or if the mailbox is not
subscribed.[¶](#section-6.3.8-2){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.8-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.8-4}
``` sourcecode
  C: A002 UNSUBSCRIBE #news.comp.mail.mime
  S: A002 OK UNSUBSCRIBE completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.8-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#list-cmd}
::: {#section-6.3.9 .section}
#### [6.3.9.](#section-6.3.9){.section-number .selfRef} [LIST Command](#name-list-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-list-command}

[]{#iref-list-command-47 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments (basic):

:   -   [reference
        name[¶](#section-6.3.9-1.2.1.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9-1.2.1.1}
    -   [mailbox name with possible
        wildcards[¶](#section-6.3.9-1.2.1.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9-1.2.1.2}

:   

Arguments (extended):

:   -   [selection options
        ([OPTIONAL]{.bcp14})[¶](#section-6.3.9-1.4.1.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9-1.4.1.1}
    -   [reference
        name[¶](#section-6.3.9-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9-1.4.1.2}
    -   [mailbox
        patterns[¶](#section-6.3.9-1.4.1.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9-1.4.1.3}
    -   [return options
        ([OPTIONAL]{.bcp14})[¶](#section-6.3.9-1.4.1.4){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9-1.4.1.4}

:   

Responses:
:   untagged responses: LIST[¶](#section-6.3.9-1.6){.pilcrow}
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   list completed[¶](#section-6.3.9-1.8.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   list failure: can\'t list that reference or mailbox
        name[¶](#section-6.3.9-1.8.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.9-1.8.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The LIST command returns a subset of mailbox names from the complete set
of all mailbox names available to the client. Zero or more untagged LIST
responses are returned, containing the name attributes, hierarchy
delimiter, name, and possible extension information; see the description
of the LIST response ([Section 7.3.1](#list-resp){.xref}) for more
detail.[¶](#section-6.3.9-2){.pilcrow}

The LIST command [SHOULD]{.bcp14} return its data quickly, without undue
delay. For example, it should not go to excess trouble to calculate the
\\Marked or \\Unmarked status or perform other processing; if each name
requires 1 second of processing, then a list of 1200 names would take 20
minutes![¶](#section-6.3.9-3){.pilcrow}

The extended LIST command, originally introduced in
\[[RFC5258](#RFC5258){.xref}\], provides capabilities beyond that of the
original IMAP LIST command. The extended syntax is being used if one or
more of the following conditions is true:[¶](#section-6.3.9-4){.pilcrow}

1.  [the first word after the command name begins with a parenthesis
    (\"LIST selection
    options\");[¶](#section-6.3.9-5.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9-5.1}
2.  [the second word after the command name begins with a parenthesis;
    and[¶](#section-6.3.9-5.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9-5.2}
3.  [the LIST command has more than 2 parameters (\"LIST return
    options\").[¶](#section-6.3.9-5.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9-5.3}

An empty (\"\" string) reference name argument indicates that the
mailbox name is interpreted as by SELECT. The returned mailbox names
[MUST]{.bcp14} match the supplied mailbox name pattern(s). A non-empty
reference name argument is the name of a mailbox or a level of mailbox
hierarchy, and it indicates the context in which the mailbox name is
interpreted. Clients [SHOULD]{.bcp14} use the empty reference
argument.[¶](#section-6.3.9-6){.pilcrow}

In the basic syntax only, an empty (\"\" string) mailbox name argument
is a special request to return the hierarchy delimiter and the root name
of the name given in the reference. The value returned as the root
[MAY]{.bcp14} be the empty string if the reference is non-rooted or is
an empty string. In all cases, a hierarchy delimiter (or NIL if there is
no hierarchy) is returned. This permits a client to get the hierarchy
delimiter (or find out that the mailbox names are flat) even when no
mailboxes by that name currently exist.[¶](#section-6.3.9-7){.pilcrow}

In the extended syntax, any mailbox name arguments that are empty
strings are ignored. There is no special meaning for empty mailbox names
when the extended syntax is used.[¶](#section-6.3.9-8){.pilcrow}

The reference and mailbox name arguments are interpreted into a
canonical form that represents an unambiguous left-to-right hierarchy.
The returned mailbox names will be in the interpreted form, which we
call a \"canonical LIST pattern\": the canonical pattern constructed
internally by the server from the reference and mailbox name
arguments.[¶](#section-6.3.9-9){.pilcrow}

Note: The interpretation of the reference argument is implementation
defined. It depends on whether the server implementation has a concept
of the \"current working directory\" and leading \"break out
characters\", which override the current working
directory.[¶](#section-6.3.9-10){.pilcrow}

For example, on a server that exports a UNIX or NT file system, the
reference argument contains the current working directory, and the
mailbox name argument contains the name as interpreted in the current
working directory.[¶](#section-6.3.9-11){.pilcrow}

If a server implementation has no concept of break out characters, the
canonical form is normally the reference name appended with the mailbox
name. Note that if the server implements the namespace convention
([Section 5.1.2.1](#namespace-convention){.xref}), \"#\" is a break out
character and must be treated as such.[¶](#section-6.3.9-12){.pilcrow}

If the reference argument is not a level of mailbox hierarchy (that is,
it is a \\NoInferiors name), and/or the reference argument does not end
with the hierarchy delimiter, it is interpreted as implementation
dependent. For example, a reference of \"foo/bar\" and mailbox name of
\"rag/baz\" could be interpreted as \"foo/bar/rag/baz\",
\"foo/barrag/baz\", or \"foo/rag/baz\". A client [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14}
use such a reference argument except at the explicit request of the
user. A hierarchical browser [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} make any assumptions
about server interpretation of the reference unless the reference is a
level of mailbox hierarchy AND ends with the hierarchy
delimiter.[¶](#section-6.3.9-13){.pilcrow}

Any part of the reference argument that is included in the interpreted
form [SHOULD]{.bcp14} prefix the interpreted form. It [SHOULD]{.bcp14}
also be in the same form as the reference name argument. This rule
permits the client to determine if the returned mailbox name is in the
context of the reference argument or if something about the mailbox
argument overrode the reference argument. Without this rule, the client
would have to have knowledge of the server\'s naming semantics including
what characters are \"breakouts\" that override a naming
context.[¶](#section-6.3.9-14){.pilcrow}

Here are some examples of how references and mailbox names might be
interpreted on a UNIX-based server:[¶](#section-6.3.9-15){.pilcrow}

::: {#table_1}
  Reference       Mailbox Name     Interpretation
  --------------- ---------------- ---------------------
  \~smith/Mail/   foo.\*           \~smith/Mail/foo.\*
  archive/        \%               archive/%
  #news.          comp.mail.\*     #news.comp.mail.\*
  \~smith/Mail/   /usr/doc/foo     /usr/doc/foo
  archive/        \~fred/Mail/\*   \~fred/Mail/\*

  : [Table 1](#table-1){.selfRef}
:::

The first three examples above demonstrate interpretations in the
context of the reference argument. Note that \"\~smith/Mail\" [SHOULD
NOT]{.bcp14} be transformed into something like
\"/u2/users/smith/Mail\", or it would be impossible for the client to
determine that the interpretation was in the context of the
reference.[¶](#section-6.3.9-17){.pilcrow}

The character \"\*\" is a wildcard and matches zero or more characters
at this position. The character \"%\" is similar to \"\*\", but it does
not match a hierarchy delimiter. If the \"%\" wildcard is the last
character of a mailbox name argument, matching levels of hierarchy are
also returned. If these levels of hierarchy are not also selectable
mailboxes, they are returned with the \\Noselect mailbox name attribute
(see the description of the LIST response ([Section
7.3.1](#list-resp){.xref}) for more
details).[¶](#section-6.3.9-18){.pilcrow}

Any syntactically valid pattern that is not accepted by a server for any
reason [MUST]{.bcp14} be silently ignored, i.e., it results in no LIST
responses, and the LIST command still returns a tagged OK
response.[¶](#section-6.3.9-19){.pilcrow}

Selection options tell the server to limit the mailbox names that are
selected by the LIST operation. If selection options are used, the
mailboxes returned are those that match both the list of canonical LIST
patterns and the selection options. Unless a particular selection option
provides special rules, the selection options are cumulative: a mailbox
that matches the mailbox patterns is selected only if it also matches
all of the selection options. (An example of a selection option with
special rules is the RECURSIVEMATCH
option.)[¶](#section-6.3.9-20){.pilcrow}

Return options control what information is returned for each matched
mailbox. Return options [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} cause the server to report
information about additional mailbox names other than those that match
the canonical LIST patterns and selection options. If no return options
are specified, the client is only expecting information about mailbox
attributes. The server [MAY]{.bcp14} return other information about the
matched mailboxes, and clients [MUST]{.bcp14} be able to handle that
situation.[¶](#section-6.3.9-21){.pilcrow}

Initial selection options and return options are defined in the
following subsections, and new ones will also be defined in extensions.
Initial options defined in this document [MUST]{.bcp14} be supported.
Each non-initial option will be enabled by a capability string (one
capability may enable multiple options), and a client [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
send an option for which the server has not advertised support. A server
[MUST]{.bcp14} respond to options it does not recognize with a BAD
response. The client [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14} specify any option more than
once; however, if the client does this, the server [MUST]{.bcp14} act as
if it received the option only once. The order in which options are
specified by the client is not
significant.[¶](#section-6.3.9-22){.pilcrow}

In general, each selection option except RECURSIVEMATCH will have a
corresponding return option with the same name. The REMOTE selection
option is an anomaly in this regard and does not have a corresponding
return option. That is because it expands, rather than restricts, the
set of mailboxes that are returned. Future extensions to this
specification should keep this parallelism in mind and define a pair of
corresponding selection and return
options.[¶](#section-6.3.9-23){.pilcrow}

Server implementations are permitted to \"hide\" otherwise accessible
mailboxes from the wildcard characters, by preventing certain characters
or names from matching a wildcard in certain situations. For example, a
UNIX-based server might restrict the interpretation of \"\*\" so that an
initial \"/\" character does not match.[¶](#section-6.3.9-24){.pilcrow}

The special name INBOX is included in the output from LIST, if INBOX is
supported by this server for this user and if the uppercase string
\"INBOX\" matches the interpreted reference and mailbox name arguments
with wildcards as described above. The criteria for omitting INBOX is
whether SELECT INBOX will return a failure; it is not relevant whether
the user\'s real INBOX resides on this or some other
server.[¶](#section-6.3.9-25){.pilcrow}

::: {#list-select-options}
::: {#section-6.3.9.1 .section}
##### [6.3.9.1.](#section-6.3.9.1){.section-number .selfRef} [LIST Selection Options](#name-list-selection-options){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-list-selection-options}

The selection options defined in this specification are as
follows:[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-1){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

SUBSCRIBED

:   Causes the LIST command to list subscribed names rather than the
    existing mailboxes. This will often be a subset of the actual
    mailboxes. It\'s also possible for this list to contain the names of
    mailboxes that don\'t exist. In any case, the list [MUST]{.bcp14}
    include exactly those mailbox names that match the canonical list
    pattern and are subscribed to.[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.2.1){.pilcrow}

    This option defines a mailbox attribute, \"\\Subscribed\", that
    indicates that a mailbox name is subscribed to. The \"\\Subscribed\"
    attribute [MUST]{.bcp14} be supported and [MUST]{.bcp14} be
    accurately computed when the SUBSCRIBED selection option is
    specified.[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.2.2){.pilcrow}

    Note that the SUBSCRIBED selection option implies the SUBSCRIBED
    return option (see below).[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.2.3){.pilcrow}

:   

REMOTE

:   Causes the LIST command to show remote mailboxes as well as local
    ones, as described in \[[RFC2193](#RFC2193){.xref}\]. This option is
    intended to replace the RLIST command and, in conjunction with the
    SUBSCRIBED selection option, the RLSUB command. Servers that don\'t
    support the concept of remote mailboxes can ignore this
    option.[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.4.1){.pilcrow}

    This option defines a mailbox attribute, \"\\Remote\", that
    indicates that a mailbox is a remote mailbox. The \"\\Remote\"
    attribute [MUST]{.bcp14} be accurately computed when the REMOTE
    option is specified.[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.4.2){.pilcrow}

    The REMOTE selection option has no interaction with other options.
    Its effect is to tell the server to apply the other options, if any,
    to remote mailboxes, in addition to local ones. In particular, it
    has no interaction with RECURSIVEMATCH (see below). A request for
    (REMOTE RECURSIVEMATCH) is invalid, because a request for
    (RECURSIVEMATCH) is also invalid. A request for (REMOTE
    RECURSIVEMATCH SUBSCRIBED) is asking for all subscribed mailboxes,
    both local and remote.[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.4.3){.pilcrow}

:   

RECURSIVEMATCH

:   Forces the server to return information about parent mailboxes that
    don\'t match other selection options but have some submailboxes that
    do. Information about children is returned in the CHILDINFO extended
    data item, as described in [Section
    6.3.9.6](#childinfo){.xref}.[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.6.1){.pilcrow}

    []{.break}

    Note 1:
    :   In order for a parent mailbox to be returned, it still has to
        match the canonical LIST
        pattern.[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.6.2.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    Note 2:
    :   When returning the CHILDINFO extended data item, it doesn\'t
        matter whether or not the submailbox matches the canonical LIST
        pattern. See also Example 9 in [Section
        6.3.9.8](#examples){.xref}.[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.6.2.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    The RECURSIVEMATCH option [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} occur as the only
    selection option (or only with REMOTE), as it only makes sense when
    other selection options are also used. The server [MUST]{.bcp14}
    return a BAD tagged response in such
    case.[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.6.3){.pilcrow}

    Note that even if the RECURSIVEMATCH option is specified, the client
    [MUST]{.bcp14} still be able to handle cases when a CHILDINFO
    extended data item is returned and there are no submailboxes that
    meet the selection criteria of the subsequent LIST command, as they
    can be deleted/renamed after the LIST response was sent but before
    the client had a chance to access
    them.[¶](#section-6.3.9.1-2.6.4){.pilcrow}

:   
:::
:::

::: {#list-return-options}
::: {#section-6.3.9.2 .section}
##### [6.3.9.2.](#section-6.3.9.2){.section-number .selfRef} [LIST Return Options](#name-list-return-options){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-list-return-options}

The return options defined in this specification are as
follows:[¶](#section-6.3.9.2-1){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

SUBSCRIBED

:   Causes the LIST command to return subscription state for all
    matching mailbox names. The \"\\Subscribed\" attribute
    [MUST]{.bcp14} be supported and [MUST]{.bcp14} be accurately
    computed when the SUBSCRIBED return option is specified.
    Furthermore, all other mailbox attributes [MUST]{.bcp14} be
    accurately computed (this differs from the behavior of the obsolete
    LSUB command from \[[RFC3501](#RFC3501){.xref}\]). Note that the
    above requirements don\'t override the requirement for the LIST
    command to return results quickly (see [Section
    6.3.9](#list-cmd){.xref}), i.e., server implementations need to
    compute results quickly and accurately. For example, server
    implementors might need to create quick access
    indices.[¶](#section-6.3.9.2-2.2.1){.pilcrow}

:   

CHILDREN
:   Requests mailbox child information as originally proposed in
    \[[RFC3348](#RFC3348){.xref}\]. See [Section
    6.3.9.5](#children){.xref}, below, for
    details.[¶](#section-6.3.9.2-2.4){.pilcrow}
:   

STATUS

:   Requests STATUS response for each matching
    mailbox.[¶](#section-6.3.9.2-2.6.1){.pilcrow}

    This option takes STATUS data items as parameters. For each
    selectable mailbox matching the list pattern and selection options,
    the server [MUST]{.bcp14} return an untagged LIST response followed
    by an untagged STATUS response containing the information requested
    in the STATUS return option, except for some cases described
    below.[¶](#section-6.3.9.2-2.6.2){.pilcrow}

    If an attempted STATUS for a listed mailbox fails because the
    mailbox can\'t be selected (e.g., if the \"l\" Access Control List
    (ACL) right \[[RFC4314](#RFC4314){.xref}\] is granted to the mailbox
    and the \"r\" right is not granted, or is due to a race condition
    between LIST and STATUS changing the mailbox to \\NoSelect), the
    STATUS response [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} be returned, and the LIST
    response [MUST]{.bcp14} include the \\NoSelect attribute. This means
    the server may have to buffer the LIST reply until it has
    successfully looked up the necessary STATUS
    information.[¶](#section-6.3.9.2-2.6.3){.pilcrow}

    If the server runs into unexpected problems while trying to look up
    the STATUS information, it [MAY]{.bcp14} drop the corresponding
    STATUS reply. In such a situation, the LIST command would still
    return a tagged OK reply.[¶](#section-6.3.9.2-2.6.4){.pilcrow}

    See the note in the discussion of the STATUS command in [Section
    6.3.11](#status-command){.xref} for information about obtaining
    status on the currently selected
    mailbox.[¶](#section-6.3.9.2-2.6.5){.pilcrow}

:   
:::
:::

::: {#general}
::: {#section-6.3.9.3 .section}
##### [6.3.9.3.](#section-6.3.9.3){.section-number .selfRef} [General Principles for Returning LIST Responses](#name-general-principles-for-retu){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-general-principles-for-retu}

This section outlines several principles that can be used by server
implementations of this document to decide whether a LIST response
should be returned, as well as how many responses and what kind of
information they may contain.[¶](#section-6.3.9.3-1){.pilcrow}

1.  [At most, one LIST response should be returned for each mailbox name
    that matches the canonical LIST pattern. Server implementors must
    not assume that clients will be able to assemble mailbox attributes
    and other information returned in multiple LIST
    responses.[¶](#section-6.3.9.3-2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9.3-2.1}

2.  ::: {#section-6.3.9.3-2.2}
    There are only two reasons for including a matching mailbox name in
    the responses to the LIST command (note that the server is allowed
    to return unsolicited responses at any time, and such responses are
    not governed by this rule):[¶](#section-6.3.9.3-2.2.1){.pilcrow}

    A.  [The mailbox name also satisfies the selection
        criteria.[¶](#section-6.3.9.3-2.2.2.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.3.9.3-2.2.2.1}

    B.  ::: {#section-6.3.9.3-2.2.2.2}
        The mailbox name doesn\'t satisfy the selection criteria, but it
        has at least one descendant mailbox name that satisfies the
        selection criteria and that doesn\'t match the canonical LIST
        pattern.[¶](#section-6.3.9.3-2.2.2.2.1){.pilcrow}

        For more information on this case, see the CHILDINFO extended
        data item described in [Section 6.3.9.6](#childinfo){.xref}.
        Note that the CHILDINFO extended data item can only be returned
        when the RECURSIVEMATCH selection option is
        specified.[¶](#section-6.3.9.3-2.2.2.2.2){.pilcrow}
        :::
    :::

3.  ::: {#section-6.3.9.3-2.3}
    Attributes returned in the same LIST response are treated
    additively. For example, the following
    response[¶](#section-6.3.9.3-2.3.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.3-2.3.2}
    ``` sourcecode
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed \NonExistent) "/" "Fruit/Peach"
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.3-2.3.2){.pilcrow}
    :::

    means that the \"Fruit/Peach\" mailbox doesn\'t exist, but it is
    subscribed.[¶](#section-6.3.9.3-2.3.3){.pilcrow}
    :::
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.3.9.4 .section}
##### [6.3.9.4.](#section-6.3.9.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Additional LIST-Related Requirements on Clients](#name-additional-list-related-req){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-additional-list-related-req}

All clients [MUST]{.bcp14} treat a LIST attribute with a stronger
meaning as implying any attribute that can be inferred from it. (See
[Section 7.3.1](#list-resp){.xref} for the list of currently defined
attributes.) For example, the client must treat the presence of the
\\NoInferiors attribute as if the \\HasNoChildren attribute was also
sent by the server.[¶](#section-6.3.9.4-1){.pilcrow}

The following table summarizes inference
rules.[¶](#section-6.3.9.4-2){.pilcrow}

  returned attribute   implied attribute
  -------------------- -------------------
  \\NoInferiors        \\HasNoChildren
  \\NonExistent        \\NoSelect

  : [Table 2](#table-2){.selfRef}
:::

::: {#children}
::: {#section-6.3.9.5 .section}
##### [6.3.9.5.](#section-6.3.9.5){.section-number .selfRef} [The CHILDREN Return Option](#name-the-children-return-option){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-the-children-return-option}

The CHILDREN return option is simply an indication that the client wants
information about whether or not mailboxes contain child mailboxes; a
server [MAY]{.bcp14} provide it even if the option is not
specified.[¶](#section-6.3.9.5-1){.pilcrow}

Many IMAP clients present the user with a hierarchical view of the
mailboxes that a user has access to. Rather than initially presenting
the entire mailbox hierarchy to the user, it is often preferable to show
the user a collapsed outline list of the mailbox hierarchy (particularly
if there is a large number of mailboxes). The user can then expand the
collapsed outline hierarchy as needed. It is common to include a visual
clue (such as a \'\'+\'\') within the collapsed hierarchy to indicate
that there are child mailboxes under a particular mailbox. When the
visual clue is clicked, the hierarchy list is expanded to show the child
mailboxes. The CHILDREN return option provides a mechanism for a client
to efficiently determine whether a particular mailbox has children,
without issuing a LIST \"\" \* or a LIST \"\" % for each mailbox name.
The CHILDREN return option defines two new attributes that
[MUST]{.bcp14} be returned within a LIST response: \\HasChildren and
\\HasNoChildren. Although these attributes [MAY]{.bcp14} be returned in
response to any LIST command, the CHILDREN return option is provided to
indicate that the client particularly wants this information. If the
CHILDREN return option is present, the server [MUST]{.bcp14} return
these attributes even if their computation is
expensive.[¶](#section-6.3.9.5-2){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

\\HasChildren
:   The presence of this attribute indicates that the mailbox has child
    mailboxes. A server [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14} set this attribute if there
    are child mailboxes and the user does not have permission to access
    any of them. In this case, \\HasNoChildren [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be used.
    In many cases, however, a server may not be able to efficiently
    compute whether a user has access to any child mailbox. Note that
    even though the \\HasChildren attribute for a mailbox must be
    correct at the time of processing the mailbox, a client must be
    prepared to deal with a situation when a mailbox is marked with the
    \\HasChildren attribute, but no child mailbox appears in the
    response to the LIST command. This might happen, for example, due to
    child mailboxes being deleted or made inaccessible to the user
    (using access control) by another client before the server is able
    to list them.[¶](#section-6.3.9.5-3.2){.pilcrow}
:   

\\HasNoChildren
:   The presence of this attribute indicates that the mailbox has NO
    child mailboxes that are accessible to the currently authenticated
    user.[¶](#section-6.3.9.5-3.4){.pilcrow}
:   

It is an error for the server to return both a \\HasChildren and a
\\HasNoChildren attribute in the same LIST
response.[¶](#section-6.3.9.5-4){.pilcrow}

Note: the \\HasNoChildren attribute should not be confused with the
\\NoInferiors attribute, which indicates that no child mailboxes exist
now and none can be created in the
future.[¶](#section-6.3.9.5-5){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#childinfo}
::: {#section-6.3.9.6 .section}
##### [6.3.9.6.](#section-6.3.9.6){.section-number .selfRef} [CHILDINFO Extended Data Item](#name-childinfo-extended-data-ite){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-childinfo-extended-data-ite}

The CHILDINFO extended data item [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} be returned unless
the client has specified the RECURSIVEMATCH selection
option.[¶](#section-6.3.9.6-1){.pilcrow}

The CHILDINFO extended data item in a LIST response describes the
selection criteria that has caused it to be returned and indicates that
the mailbox has at least one descendant mailbox that matches the
selection criteria.[¶](#section-6.3.9.6-2){.pilcrow}

Note: Some servers allow for mailboxes to exist without requiring their
parent to exist. For example, the mailbox \"Customers/ABC\" can exist
while the mailbox \"Customers\" does not. As the CHILDINFO extended data
item is not allowed if the RECURSIVEMATCH selection option is not
specified, such servers [SHOULD]{.bcp14} use the \"\\NonExistent
\\HasChildren\" attribute pair to signal to the client that there is a
descendant mailbox that matches the selection criteria. See Example 11
in [Section 6.3.9.8](#examples){.xref}.[¶](#section-6.3.9.6-3){.pilcrow}

The returned selection criteria allows the client to distinguish a
solicited response from an unsolicited one, as well as to distinguish
among solicited responses caused by multiple pipelined LIST commands
that specify different criteria.[¶](#section-6.3.9.6-4){.pilcrow}

Servers [SHOULD]{.bcp14} only return a non-matching mailbox name along
with CHILDINFO if at least one matching child is not also being
returned. That is, servers [SHOULD]{.bcp14} suppress redundant CHILDINFO
responses.[¶](#section-6.3.9.6-5){.pilcrow}

Examples 8 and 10 in [Section 6.3.9.8](#examples){.xref} demonstrate the
difference between the present CHILDINFO extended data item and the
\"\\HasChildren\" attribute.[¶](#section-6.3.9.6-6){.pilcrow}

The following table summarizes interaction between the \"\\NonExistent\"
attribute and CHILDINFO (the first column indicates whether the parent
mailbox exists):[¶](#section-6.3.9.6-7){.pilcrow}

  Exists   Meets the selection criteria   Has a child that meets the selection criteria   Returned IMAP4rev2/LIST-EXTENDED attributes and CHILDINFO
  -------- ------------------------------ ----------------------------------------------- -----------------------------------------------------------
  no       no                             no                                              no LIST response returned
  yes      no                             no                                              no LIST response returned
  no       yes                            no                                              (\\NonExistent \<attr>)
  yes      yes                            no                                              (\<attr>)
  no       no                             yes                                             (\\NonExistent) + CHILDINFO
  yes      no                             yes                                             () + CHILDINFO
  no       yes                            yes                                             (\\NonExistent \<attr>) + CHILDINFO
  yes      yes                            yes                                             (\<attr>) + CHILDINFO

  : [Table 3](#table-3){.selfRef}

where \<attr> is one or more attributes that correspond to the selection
criteria; for example, for the SUBSCRIBED option, the \<attr> is
\\Subscribed.[¶](#section-6.3.9.6-9){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#oldname}
::: {#section-6.3.9.7 .section}
##### [6.3.9.7.](#section-6.3.9.7){.section-number .selfRef} [OLDNAME Extended Data Item](#name-oldname-extended-data-item){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-oldname-extended-data-item}

The OLDNAME extended data item is included when a mailbox name is
created (with the CREATE command), renamed (with the RENAME command), or
deleted (with the DELETE command). (When a mailbox is deleted, the
\"\\NonExistent\" attribute is also included.) IMAP extensions can
specify other conditions when the OLDNAME extended data item should be
included.[¶](#section-6.3.9.7-1){.pilcrow}

If the server allows denormalized mailbox names (see [Section
5.1](#mailbox-naming){.xref}) in SELECT/EXAMINE, CREATE, RENAME, or
DELETE, it [SHOULD]{.bcp14} return an unsolicited LIST response that
includes the OLDNAME extended data item, whenever the supplied mailbox
name differs from the resulting normalized mailbox name. From the client
point of view, this is indistinguishable from another user renaming or
deleting the mailbox, as specified in the previous
paragraph.[¶](#section-6.3.9.7-2){.pilcrow}

A deleted mailbox can be announced as
follows:[¶](#section-6.3.9.7-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.9.7-4}
``` sourcecode
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent) "." "INBOX.DeletedMailbox"
```

[¶](#section-6.3.9.7-4){.pilcrow}
:::

Example of a renamed mailbox:[¶](#section-6.3.9.7-5){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.9.7-6}
``` sourcecode
  S: * LIST () "/" "NewMailbox" ("OLDNAME" ("OldMailbox"))
```

[¶](#section-6.3.9.7-6){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::

::: {#examples}
::: {#section-6.3.9.8 .section}
##### [6.3.9.8.](#section-6.3.9.8){.section-number .selfRef} [LIST Command Examples](#name-list-command-examples){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-list-command-examples}

This example shows some uses of the basic LIST
command:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-1){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-2){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.9.8-3}
``` sourcecode
  C: A101 LIST "" ""
  S: * LIST (\Noselect) "/" ""
  S: A101 OK LIST Completed
  C: A102 LIST #news.comp.mail.misc ""
  S: * LIST (\Noselect) "." #news.
  S: A102 OK LIST Completed
  C: A103 LIST /usr/staff/jones ""
  S: * LIST (\Noselect) "/" /
  S: A103 OK LIST Completed
  C: A202 LIST ~/Mail/ %
  S: * LIST (\Noselect) "/" ~/Mail/foo
  S: * LIST () "/" ~/Mail/meetings
  S: A202 OK LIST completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-3){.pilcrow}
:::

Extended examples:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-4){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

1:

:   The first example shows the complete local hierarchy that will be
    used for the other examples.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.1.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.1.2}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A01 LIST "" "*"
      S: * LIST (\Marked \NoInferiors) "/" "inbox"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Fruit"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Fruit/Apple"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Fruit/Banana"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Tofu"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Vegetable"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Vegetable/Broccoli"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Vegetable/Corn"
      S: A01 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :::

:   

2:

:   In the next example, we will see the subscribed mailboxes. This is
    similar to, but not equivalent with, the now deprecated \<LSUB \"\"
    \"\*\"\> (see \[[RFC3501](#RFC3501){.xref}\] for more details on the
    LSUB command). Note that the mailbox called \"Fruit/Peach\" is
    subscribed to, but it does not actually exist (perhaps it was
    deleted while still subscribed). The \"Fruit\" mailbox is not
    subscribed to, but it has two subscribed children. The \"Vegetable\"
    mailbox is subscribed and has two children; one of them is
    subscribed as well.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.2.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.2.2}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A02 LIST (SUBSCRIBED) "" "*"
      S: * LIST (\Marked \NoInferiors \Subscribed) "/" "inbox"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Fruit/Banana"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed \NonExistent) "/" "Fruit/Peach"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Vegetable"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Vegetable/Broccoli"
      S: A02 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.2.2){.pilcrow}
    :::

:   

3:

:   The next example shows the use of the CHILDREN option. The client,
    without having to list the second level of hierarchy, now knows
    which of the top-level mailboxes have submailboxes (children) and
    which do not. Note that it\'s not necessary for the server to return
    the \\HasNoChildren attribute for the inbox, because the
    \\NoInferiors attribute already implies that and has a stronger
    meaning.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.3.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.3.2}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A03 LIST () "" "%" RETURN (CHILDREN)
      S: * LIST (\Marked \NoInferiors) "/" "inbox"
      S: * LIST (\HasChildren) "/" "Fruit"
      S: * LIST (\HasNoChildren) "/" "Tofu"
      S: * LIST (\HasChildren) "/" "Vegetable"
      S: A03 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.3.2){.pilcrow}
    :::

:   

4:

:   In this example, we see more mailboxes that reside on another
    server. This is similar to the command \<RLIST \"\"
    \"%\"\>.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.4.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.4.2}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A04 LIST (REMOTE) "" "%" RETURN (CHILDREN)
      S: * LIST (\Marked \NoInferiors) "/" "inbox"
      S: * LIST (\HasChildren) "/" "Fruit"
      S: * LIST (\HasNoChildren) "/" "Tofu"
      S: * LIST (\HasChildren) "/" "Vegetable"
      S: * LIST (\Remote \HasNoChildren) "/" "Bread"
      S: * LIST (\HasChildren \Remote) "/" "Meat"
      S: A04 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.4.2){.pilcrow}
    :::

:   

5:

:   The following example also requests the server to include mailboxes
    that reside on another server. The server returns information about
    all mailboxes that are subscribed. This is similar to the command
    \<RLSUB \"\" \"\*\"\> (see \[[RFC2193](#RFC2193){.xref}\] for more
    details on RLSUB). We also see the use of two selection
    options.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.5.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.5.2}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A05 LIST (REMOTE SUBSCRIBED) "" "*"
      S: * LIST (\Marked \NoInferiors \Subscribed) "/" "inbox"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Fruit/Banana"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed \NonExistent) "/" "Fruit/Peach"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Vegetable"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Vegetable/Broccoli"
      S: * LIST (\Remote \Subscribed) "/" "Bread"
      S: A05 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.5.2){.pilcrow}
    :::

:   

6:

:   The following example requests the server to include mailboxes that
    reside on another server. The server is asked to return subscription
    information for all returned mailboxes. This is different from the
    example above.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.6.1){.pilcrow}

    Note that the output of this command is not a superset of the output
    in the previous example, as it doesn\'t include a LIST response for
    the non-existent
    \"Fruit/Peach\".[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.6.2){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.6.3}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A06 LIST (REMOTE) "" "*" RETURN (SUBSCRIBED)
      S: * LIST (\Marked \NoInferiors \Subscribed) "/" "inbox"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Fruit"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Fruit/Apple"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Fruit/Banana"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Tofu"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Vegetable"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Vegetable/Broccoli"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Vegetable/Corn"
      S: * LIST (\Remote \Subscribed) "/" "Bread"
      S: * LIST (\Remote) "/" "Meat"
      S: A06 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.6.3){.pilcrow}
    :::

:   

7:

:   The following example demonstrates the difference between the
    \\HasChildren attribute and the CHILDINFO extended data
    item.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.1){.pilcrow}

    Let\'s assume there is the following
    hierarchy:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.2){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.3}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: C01 LIST "" "*"
      S: * LIST (\Marked \NoInferiors) "/" "inbox"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Foo"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Foo/Bar"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Foo/Baz"
      S: * LIST () "/" "Moo"
      S: C01 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.3){.pilcrow}
    :::

    If the client asks RETURN (CHILDREN), it will get
    this:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.4){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.5}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: CA3 LIST "" "%" RETURN (CHILDREN)
      S: * LIST (\Marked \NoInferiors) "/" "inbox"
      S: * LIST (\HasChildren) "/" "Foo"
      S: * LIST (\HasNoChildren) "/" "Moo"
      S: CA3 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.5){.pilcrow}
    :::

    []{.break}

    A\)

    :   Let\'s also assume that the mailbox \"Foo/Baz\" is the only
        subscribed mailbox. Then we get this
        result:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.1){.pilcrow}

        ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.2}
        ``` sourcecode
          C: C02 LIST (SUBSCRIBED) "" "*"
          S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Foo/Baz"
          S: C02 OK done
        ```

        [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
        :::

        Now, if the client issues \<LIST (SUBSCRIBED) \"\" \"%\"\>, the
        server will return no mailboxes (as the mailboxes \"Moo\",
        \"Foo\", and \"Inbox\" are NOT subscribed). However, if the
        client issues this:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.3){.pilcrow}

        ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.4}
        ``` sourcecode
          C: C04 LIST (SUBSCRIBED RECURSIVEMATCH) "" "%"
          S: * LIST () "/" "Foo" ("CHILDINFO" ("SUBSCRIBED"))
          S: C04 OK done
        ```

        [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
        :::

        (that is, the mailbox \"Foo\" is not subscribed, but it has a
        child that is), then A1 or A2
        occurs.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.5){.pilcrow}

        []{.break}

        A1)

        :   If the mailbox \"Foo\" had also been subscribed, the last
            command would return
