            this:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.6.1.1){.pilcrow}

            ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.6.1.2}
            ``` sourcecode
              C: C04 LIST (SUBSCRIBED RECURSIVEMATCH) "" "%"
              S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "Foo" ("CHILDINFO"
                  ("SUBSCRIBED"))
              S: C04 OK done
            ```

            [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
            :::

            or even this:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.6.1.3){.pilcrow}

            ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.6.1.4}
            ``` sourcecode
              C: C04 LIST (SUBSCRIBED RECURSIVEMATCH) "" "%"
              S: * LIST (\Subscribed \HasChildren) "/" "Foo"
                  ("CHILDINFO" ("SUBSCRIBED"))
              S: C04 OK done
            ```

            [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
            :::

        :   

        A2)

        :   If we assume instead that the mailbox \"Foo\" is not part of
            the original hierarchy and is not subscribed, the last
            command will give this
            result:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.6.2.1){.pilcrow}

            ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.6.2.2}
            ``` sourcecode
              C: C04 LIST (SUBSCRIBED RECURSIVEMATCH) "" "%"
              S: * LIST (\NonExistent) "/" "Foo" ("CHILDINFO"
                  ("SUBSCRIBED"))
              S: C04 OK done
            ```

            [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.1.6.2.2){.pilcrow}
            :::

        :   

    :   

    B\)

    :   Now, let\'s assume that no mailbox is subscribed. In this case,
        the command \<LIST (SUBSCRIBED RECURSIVEMATCH) \"\" \"%\"\> will
        return no responses, as there are no subscribed children (even
        though \"Foo\" has
        children).[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.2.1){.pilcrow}

    :   

    C\)

    :   And finally, suppose that only the mailboxes \"Foo\" and \"Moo\"
        are subscribed. In that case, we see this
        result:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.3.1){.pilcrow}

        ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.3.2}
        ``` sourcecode
          C: C04 LIST (SUBSCRIBED RECURSIVEMATCH) "" "%" RETURN
              (CHILDREN)
          S: * LIST (\HasChildren \Subscribed) "/" "Foo"
          S: * LIST (\HasNoChildren \Subscribed) "/" "Moo"
          S: C04 OK done
        ```

        [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.3.2){.pilcrow}
        :::

        (which means that the mailbox \"Foo\" has children, but none of
        them is subscribed).[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.7.6.3.3){.pilcrow}

    :   

:   

8:

:   The following example demonstrates that the CHILDINFO extended data
    item is returned whether or not child mailboxes match the canonical
    LIST pattern.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.1){.pilcrow}

    Let\'s assume there is the following
    hierarchy:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.2){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.3}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: D01 LIST "" "*"
      S: * LIST (\Marked \NoInferiors) "/" "inbox"
      S: * LIST () "/" "foo2"
      S: * LIST () "/" "foo2/bar1"
      S: * LIST () "/" "foo2/bar2"
      S: * LIST () "/" "baz2"
      S: * LIST () "/" "baz2/bar2"
      S: * LIST () "/" "baz2/bar22"
      S: * LIST () "/" "baz2/bar222"
      S: * LIST () "/" "eps2"
      S: * LIST () "/" "eps2/mamba"
      S: * LIST () "/" "qux2/bar2"
      S: D01 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.3){.pilcrow}
    :::

    And that the following mailboxes are
    subscribed:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.4){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.5}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: D02 LIST (SUBSCRIBED) "" "*"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "foo2/bar1"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "foo2/bar2"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "baz2/bar2"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "baz2/bar22"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "baz2/bar222"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "eps2"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "eps2/mamba"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "qux2/bar2"
      S: D02 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.5){.pilcrow}
    :::

    The client issues the following command
    first:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.6){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.7}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: D03 LIST (RECURSIVEMATCH SUBSCRIBED) "" "*2"
      S: * LIST () "/" "foo2" ("CHILDINFO" ("SUBSCRIBED"))
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "foo2/bar2"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "baz2/bar2"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "baz2/bar22"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "baz2/bar222"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "eps2" ("CHILDINFO" ("SUBSCRIBED"))
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "qux2/bar2"
      S: D03 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.7){.pilcrow}
    :::

    and the server may also include the following (but this would
    violate a restriction in [Section 6.3.9.6](#childinfo){.xref},
    because CHILDINFO is
    redundant):[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.8){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.9}
    ``` sourcecode
      S: * LIST () "/" "baz2" ("CHILDINFO" ("SUBSCRIBED"))
      S: * LIST (\NonExistent) "/" "qux2" ("CHILDINFO" ("SUBSCRIBED"))
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.9){.pilcrow}
    :::

    The CHILDINFO extended data item is returned for mailboxes \"foo2\",
    \"baz2\", and \"eps2\" because all of them have subscribed children,
    even though for the mailbox \"foo2\", only one of the two subscribed
    children matches the pattern; for the mailbox \"baz2\", all of the
    subscribed children match the pattern; and for the mailbox \"eps2\",
    none of the subscribed children match the
    pattern.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.10){.pilcrow}

    Note that if the client issues the
    following:[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.11){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.12}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: D03 LIST (RECURSIVEMATCH SUBSCRIBED) "" "*"
      S: * LIST () "/" "foo2" ("CHILDINFO" ("SUBSCRIBED"))
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "foo2/bar1"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "foo2/bar2"
      S: * LIST () "/" "baz2" ("CHILDINFO" ("SUBSCRIBED"))
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "baz2/bar2"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "baz2/bar22"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "baz2/bar222"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "eps2" ("CHILDINFO" ("SUBSCRIBED"))
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "eps2/mamba"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "/" "qux2/bar2"
      S: D03 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.12){.pilcrow}
    :::

    the LIST responses for mailboxes \"foo2\", \"baz2\", and \"eps2\"
    still have the CHILDINFO extended data item, even though this
    information is redundant and the client can determine it by
    itself.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.8.13){.pilcrow}

:   

9:

:   The following example shows usage of an extended syntax for the
    mailbox pattern. It also demonstrates that the presence of the
    CHILDINFO extended data item doesn\'t necessarily imply
    \\HasChildren.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.9.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.9.2}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: a1 LIST "" ("foo")
      S: * LIST () "/" foo
      S: a1 OK done

      C: a2 LIST (SUBSCRIBED) "" "foo/*"
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed \NonExistent) "/" foo/bar
      S: a2 OK done

      C: a3 LIST (SUBSCRIBED RECURSIVEMATCH) "" foo RETURN (CHILDREN)
      S: * LIST (\HasNoChildren) "/" foo ("CHILDINFO" ("SUBSCRIBED"))
      S: a3 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.9.2){.pilcrow}
    :::

:   

10:

:   The following example shows how a server that supports missing
    mailbox hierarchy elements can signal to a client that didn\'t
    specify the RECURSIVEMATCH selection option that there is a child
    mailbox that matches the selection
    criteria.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.10.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.10.2}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: a1 LIST (REMOTE) "" *
      S: * LIST () "/" music/rock
      S: * LIST (\Remote) "/" also/jazz
      S: a1 OK done

      C: a2 LIST () "" %
      S: * LIST (\NonExistent \HasChildren) "/" music
      S: a2 OK done

      C: a3 LIST (REMOTE) "" %
      S: * LIST (\NonExistent \HasChildren) "/" music
      S: * LIST (\NonExistent \HasChildren) "/" also
      S: a3 OK done

      C: a3.1 LIST "" (% music/rock)
      S: * LIST () "/" music/rock
      S: a3.1 OK done
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.10.2){.pilcrow}
    :::

    Because \"music/rock\" is the only mailbox under \"music\", there\'s
    no need for the server to also return \"music\". However, clients
    must handle both cases.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.10.3){.pilcrow}

:   

11:

:   The following examples show use of the STATUS return
    option.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.11.1){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.11.2}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A01 LIST "" % RETURN (STATUS (MESSAGES UNSEEN))
      S: * LIST () "."  "INBOX"
      S: * STATUS "INBOX" (MESSAGES 17 UNSEEN 16)
      S: * LIST () "." "foo"
      S: * STATUS "foo" (MESSAGES 30 UNSEEN 29)
      S: * LIST (\NoSelect) "." "bar"
      S: A01 OK List completed.
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.11.2){.pilcrow}
    :::

    The \"bar\" mailbox isn\'t selectable, so it has no STATUS
    reply.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.11.3){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.3.9.8-5.11.4}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A02 LIST (SUBSCRIBED RECURSIVEMATCH) "" % RETURN (STATUS
           (MESSAGES))
      S: * LIST (\Subscribed) "."  "INBOX"
      S: * STATUS "INBOX" (MESSAGES 17)
      S: * LIST () "." "foo" (CHILDINFO ("SUBSCRIBED"))
      S: A02 OK List completed.
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.11.4){.pilcrow}
    :::

    The LIST reply for \"foo\" is returned because it has matching
    children, but no STATUS reply is returned because \"foo\" itself
    doesn\'t match the selection
    criteria.[¶](#section-6.3.9.8-5.11.5){.pilcrow}

:   
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.3.10 .section}
#### [6.3.10.](#section-6.3.10){.section-number .selfRef} [NAMESPACE Command](#name-namespace-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-namespace-command}

[]{#iref-namespace-command-48 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   none[¶](#section-6.3.10-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    [REQUIRED]{.bcp14} untagged responses:
    :   NAMESPACE[¶](#section-6.3.10-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   command completed[¶](#section-6.3.10-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   Can\'t complete the
        command[¶](#section-6.3.10-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   arguments invalid[¶](#section-6.3.10-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The NAMESPACE command causes a single untagged NAMESPACE response to be
returned. The untagged NAMESPACE response contains the prefix and
hierarchy delimiter to the server\'s Personal Namespace(s), Other
Users\' Namespace(s), and Shared Namespace(s) that the server wishes to
expose. The response will contain a NIL for any namespace class that is
not available. The namespace-response-extensions ABNF non-terminal is
defined for extensibility and [MAY]{.bcp14} be included in the NAMESPACE
response.[¶](#section-6.3.10-2){.pilcrow}

Example 1:[¶](#section-6.3.10-3){.pilcrow}

In this example, a server supports a single Personal Namespace. No
leading prefix is used on personal mailboxes, and \"/\" is the hierarchy
delimiter.[¶](#section-6.3.10-4){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-5}
``` sourcecode
  C: A001 NAMESPACE
  S: * NAMESPACE (("" "/")) NIL NIL
  S: A001 OK NAMESPACE command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-5){.pilcrow}
:::

Example 2:[¶](#section-6.3.10-6){.pilcrow}

A user logged on anonymously to a server. No personal mailboxes are
associated with the anonymous user, and the user does not have access to
the Other Users\' Namespace. No prefix is required to access shared
mailboxes, and the hierarchy delimiter is
\".\"[¶](#section-6.3.10-7){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-8}
``` sourcecode
  C: A001 NAMESPACE
  S: * NAMESPACE NIL NIL (("" "."))
  S: A001 OK NAMESPACE command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-8){.pilcrow}
:::

Example 3:[¶](#section-6.3.10-9){.pilcrow}

A server that contains a Personal Namespace and a single Shared
Namespace.[¶](#section-6.3.10-10){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-11}
``` sourcecode
  C: A001 NAMESPACE
  S: * NAMESPACE (("" "/")) NIL (("Public Folders/" "/"))
  S: A001 OK NAMESPACE command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-11){.pilcrow}
:::

Example 4:[¶](#section-6.3.10-12){.pilcrow}

A server that contains a Personal Namespace, Other Users\' Namespace,
and multiple Shared Namespaces. Note that the hierarchy delimiter used
within each namespace can be different.[¶](#section-6.3.10-13){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-14}
``` sourcecode
  C: A001 NAMESPACE
  S: * NAMESPACE (("" "/")) (("~" "/")) (("#shared/" "/")
      ("#public/" "/")("#ftp/" "/")("#news." "."))
  S: A001 OK NAMESPACE command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-14){.pilcrow}
:::

The prefix string allows a client to do things such as automatically
create personal mailboxes or LIST all available mailboxes within a
namespace.[¶](#section-6.3.10-15){.pilcrow}

Example 5:[¶](#section-6.3.10-16){.pilcrow}

A server that supports only the Personal Namespace, with a leading
prefix of INBOX to personal mailboxes and a hierarchy delimiter of
\".\".[¶](#section-6.3.10-17){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-18}
``` sourcecode
  C: A001 NAMESPACE
  S: * NAMESPACE (("INBOX." ".")) NIL  NIL
  S: A001 OK NAMESPACE command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-18){.pilcrow}
:::

Automatically create a mailbox to store sent
items.[¶](#section-6.3.10-19){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-20}
``` sourcecode
  C: A002 CREATE "INBOX.Sent Mail"
  S: A002 OK CREATE command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-20){.pilcrow}
:::

Although a server will typically support only a single Personal
Namespace, and a single Other User\'s Namespace, circumstances exist
where there [MAY]{.bcp14} be multiples of these, and a client
[MUST]{.bcp14} be prepared for them. If a client is configured such that
it is required to create a certain mailbox, there can be circumstances
where it is unclear which Personal Namespaces it should create the
mailbox in. In these situations, a client [SHOULD]{.bcp14} let the user
select which namespaces to create the mailbox in, or just use the first
Personal Namespace.[¶](#section-6.3.10-21){.pilcrow}

Example 6:[¶](#section-6.3.10-22){.pilcrow}

In this example, a server supports two Personal Namespaces. In addition
to the regular Personal Namespace, the user has an additional Personal
Namespace that allows access to mailboxes in an MH format
mailstore.[¶](#section-6.3.10-23){.pilcrow}

The client is configured to save a copy of all mail sent by the user
into a mailbox with the \\Sent attribute (see [Section
7.3.1](#list-resp){.xref}). Furthermore, after a message is deleted from
a mailbox, the client is configured to move that message to a mailbox
with the \\Trash attribute. The server signals with the \\NonExistent
mailbox attribute that the corresponding mailboxes don\'t exist yet and
that it is possible to create them. Once created, they could be used for
\\Sent or \\Trash purposes, and the server will no longer include the
\\NonExistent mailbox attribute for
them.[¶](#section-6.3.10-24){.pilcrow}

Note that this example demonstrates how some extension parameters can be
passed to further describe the #mh namespace. See the fictitious
\"X-PARAM\" extension parameter.[¶](#section-6.3.10-25){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-26}
``` sourcecode
  C: A001 NAMESPACE
  S: * NAMESPACE (("" "/")("#mh/" "/" "X-PARAM"
      ("FLAG1" "FLAG2"))) NIL NIL
  S: A001 OK NAMESPACE command completed

  C: A002 LIST (SPECIAL-USE) "" "*"
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent \Archive) "/" Archives
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent \Drafts) "/" Drafts
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent \Junk) "/" Junk
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent \Sent) "/" "Sent Mail"
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent \Trash) "/" "Deleted Items"
  S: A002 OK LIST Completed

  C: A003 LIST (SPECIAL-USE) "#mh/" "*"
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent \Archive) "/" "#mh/Archives"
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent \Drafts) "/" "#mh/Drafts"
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent \Junk) "/" "#mh/Junk"
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent \Sent) "/" "#mh/Sent Mail"
  S: * LIST (\NonExistent \Trash) "/" "#mh/Deleted Items"
  S: A003 OK LIST Completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-26){.pilcrow}
:::

It is desired to keep only one copy of sent mail. It is unclear which
Personal Namespace the client should use to create the \'Sent Mail\'
mailbox. The user is prompted to select a namespace, and only one \'Sent
Mail\' mailbox is created.[¶](#section-6.3.10-27){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-28}
``` sourcecode
  C: A004 CREATE "Sent Mail"
  S: A004 OK CREATE command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-28){.pilcrow}
:::

The client is designed so that it keeps two \'Deleted Items\' mailboxes,
one for each namespace.[¶](#section-6.3.10-29){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-30}
``` sourcecode
  C: A005 CREATE "Delete Items"
  S: A005 OK CREATE command completed

  C: A006 CREATE "#mh/Deleted Items"
  S: A006 OK CREATE command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-30){.pilcrow}
:::

The next level of hierarchy following the Other Users\' Namespace prefix
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} consist of \<username>, where \<username> is a user
name as per the LOGIN or AUTHENTICATE
command.[¶](#section-6.3.10-31){.pilcrow}

A client can construct a LIST command by appending a \"%\" to the Other
Users\' Namespace prefix to discover the Personal Namespaces of other
users that are available to the currently authenticated
user.[¶](#section-6.3.10-32){.pilcrow}

In response to such a LIST command, a server [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14} return
user names that have not granted access to their personal mailboxes to
the user in question.[¶](#section-6.3.10-33){.pilcrow}

A server [MAY]{.bcp14} return a LIST response containing only the names
of users that have explicitly granted access to the user in
question.[¶](#section-6.3.10-34){.pilcrow}

Alternatively, a server [MAY]{.bcp14} return NO to such a LIST command,
requiring that a user name be included with the Other Users\' Namespace
prefix before listing any other user\'s
mailboxes.[¶](#section-6.3.10-35){.pilcrow}

Example 7:[¶](#section-6.3.10-36){.pilcrow}

A server that supports providing a list of other user\'s mailboxes that
are accessible to the currently logged on
user.[¶](#section-6.3.10-37){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-38}
``` sourcecode
  C: A001 NAMESPACE
  S: * NAMESPACE (("" "/")) (("Other Users/" "/")) NIL
  S: A001 OK NAMESPACE command completed

  C: A002 LIST "" "Other Users/%"
  S: * LIST () "/" "Other Users/Mike"
  S: * LIST () "/" "Other Users/Karen"
  S: * LIST () "/" "Other Users/Matthew"
  S: * LIST () "/" "Other Users/Tesa"
  S: A002 OK LIST command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-38){.pilcrow}
:::

Example 8:[¶](#section-6.3.10-39){.pilcrow}

A server that does not support providing a list of other user\'s
mailboxes that are accessible to the currently logged on user. The
mailboxes are listable if the client includes the name of the other user
with the Other Users\' Namespace
prefix.[¶](#section-6.3.10-40){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-41}
``` sourcecode
  C: A001 NAMESPACE
  S: * NAMESPACE (("" "/")) (("#Users/" "/")) NIL
  S: A001 OK NAMESPACE command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-41){.pilcrow}
:::

In this example, the currently logged on user has access to the Personal
Namespace of user Mike, but the server chose to suppress this
information in the LIST response. However, by appending the user name
Mike (received through user input) to the Other Users\' Namespace
prefix, the client is able to get a listing of the personal mailboxes of
user Mike.[¶](#section-6.3.10-42){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-43}
``` sourcecode
  C: A002 LIST "" "#Users/%"
  S: A002 NO The requested item could not be found.

  C: A003 LIST "" "#Users/Mike/%"
  S: * LIST () "/" "#Users/Mike/INBOX"
  S: * LIST () "/" "#Users/Mike/Foo"
  S: A003 OK LIST command completed.
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-43){.pilcrow}
:::

A prefix string might not contain a hierarchy delimiter, because in some
cases, it is not needed as part of the
prefix.[¶](#section-6.3.10-44){.pilcrow}

Example 9:[¶](#section-6.3.10-45){.pilcrow}

A server that allows access to the Other Users\' Namespace by prefixing
the others\' mailboxes with a \'\~\' followed by \<username>, where
\<username> is a user name as per the LOGIN or AUTHENTICATE
command.[¶](#section-6.3.10-46){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-47}
``` sourcecode
  C: A001 NAMESPACE
  S: * NAMESPACE (("" "/")) (("~" "/")) NIL
  S: A001 OK NAMESPACE command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-47){.pilcrow}
:::

List the mailboxes for user mark[¶](#section-6.3.10-48){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.10-49}
``` sourcecode
  C: A002 LIST "" "~mark/%"
  S: * LIST () "/" "~mark/INBOX"
  S: * LIST () "/" "~mark/foo"
  S: A002 OK LIST command completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.10-49){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#status-command}
::: {#section-6.3.11 .section}
#### [6.3.11.](#section-6.3.11){.section-number .selfRef} [STATUS Command](#name-status-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-status-command}

[]{#iref-status-command-49 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:

:   mailbox name[¶](#section-6.3.11-1.2.1){.pilcrow}

    status data item names[¶](#section-6.3.11-1.2.2){.pilcrow}

:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    [REQUIRED]{.bcp14} untagged responses:
    :   STATUS[¶](#section-6.3.11-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   status completed[¶](#section-6.3.11-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   status failure: no status for that
        name[¶](#section-6.3.11-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.11-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The STATUS command requests the status of the indicated mailbox. It does
not change the currently selected mailbox, nor does it affect the state
of any messages in the queried mailbox.[¶](#section-6.3.11-2){.pilcrow}

The STATUS command provides an alternative to opening a second IMAP4rev2
connection and doing an EXAMINE command on a mailbox to query that
mailbox\'s status without deselecting the current mailbox in the first
IMAP4rev2 connection.[¶](#section-6.3.11-3){.pilcrow}

Unlike the LIST command, the STATUS command is not guaranteed to be fast
in its response. Under certain circumstances, it can be quite slow. In
some implementations, the server is obliged to open the mailbox as
\"read-only\" internally to obtain certain status information. Also
unlike the LIST command, the STATUS command does not accept
wildcards.[¶](#section-6.3.11-4){.pilcrow}

Note: The STATUS command is intended to access the status of mailboxes
other than the currently selected mailbox. Because the STATUS command
can cause the mailbox to be opened internally, and because this
information is available by other means on the selected mailbox, the
STATUS command [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14} be used on the currently selected
mailbox. However, servers [MUST]{.bcp14} be able to execute the STATUS
command on the selected mailbox. (This might also implicitly happen when
the STATUS return option is used in a LIST
command.)[¶](#section-6.3.11-5){.pilcrow}

The STATUS command [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} be used as a \"check for new
messages in the selected mailbox\" operation (refer to Sections
[7](#server-responses){.xref} and [7.4.1](#exists){.xref} for more
information about the proper method for new message
checking).[¶](#section-6.3.11-6){.pilcrow}

STATUS SIZE (see below) can take a significant amount of time, depending
upon server implementation. Clients should use STATUS SIZE
cautiously.[¶](#section-6.3.11-7){.pilcrow}

The currently defined status data items that can be requested
are:[¶](#section-6.3.11-8){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

MESSAGES
:   []{#iref-messages-status-item-50 .iref} The number of messages in
    the mailbox.[¶](#section-6.3.11-9.2){.pilcrow}
:   

UIDNEXT
:   []{#iref-uidnext-status-item-51 .iref} The next unique identifier
    value of the mailbox. Refer to [Section 2.3.1.1](#uid-def){.xref}
    for more information.[¶](#section-6.3.11-9.4){.pilcrow}
:   

UIDVALIDITY
:   []{#iref-uidvalidity-status-item-52 .iref} The unique identifier
    validity value of the mailbox. Refer to [Section
    2.3.1.1](#uid-def){.xref} for more
    information.[¶](#section-6.3.11-9.6){.pilcrow}
:   

UNSEEN
:   []{#iref-unseen-status-item-53 .iref} The number of messages that do
    not have the \\Seen flag set.[¶](#section-6.3.11-9.8){.pilcrow}
:   

DELETED
:   []{#iref-deleted-status-item-54 .iref} The number of messages that
    have the \\Deleted flag set.[¶](#section-6.3.11-9.10){.pilcrow}
:   

SIZE
:   []{#iref-size-status-item-55 .iref} The total size of the mailbox in
    octets. This is not strictly required to be an exact value, but it
    [MUST]{.bcp14} be equal to or greater than the sum of the values of
    the RFC822.SIZE FETCH message data items (see [Section
    6.4.5](#fetch-command){.xref}) of all messages in the
    mailbox.[¶](#section-6.3.11-9.12){.pilcrow}
:   

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.11-10){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.11-11}
``` sourcecode
  C: A042 STATUS blurdybloop (UIDNEXT MESSAGES)
  S: * STATUS blurdybloop (MESSAGES 231 UIDNEXT 44292)
  S: A042 OK STATUS completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.11-11){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.3.12 .section}
#### [6.3.12.](#section-6.3.12){.section-number .selfRef} [APPEND Command](#name-append-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-append-command}

[]{#iref-append-command-56 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:

:   mailbox name[¶](#section-6.3.12-1.2.1){.pilcrow}

    [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} flag parenthesized
    list[¶](#section-6.3.12-1.2.2){.pilcrow}

    [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} date/time
    string[¶](#section-6.3.12-1.2.3){.pilcrow}

    message literal[¶](#section-6.3.12-1.2.4){.pilcrow}

:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} untagged response:
    :   LIST[¶](#section-6.3.12-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   append completed[¶](#section-6.3.12-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   append error: can\'t append to that mailbox, error in flags or
        date/time or message text[¶](#section-6.3.12-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.12-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The APPEND command appends the literal argument as a new message to the
end of the specified destination mailbox. This argument [SHOULD]{.bcp14}
be in the format of an \[[RFC5322](#RFC5322){.xref}\] or
\[[I18N-HDRS](#RFC6532){.xref}\] message. 8-bit characters are permitted
in the message. A server implementation that is unable to preserve 8-bit
data properly [MUST]{.bcp14} be able to reversibly convert 8-bit APPEND
data to 7 bits using a \[[MIME-IMB](#RFC2045){.xref}\] content transfer
encoding.[¶](#section-6.3.12-2){.pilcrow}

Note: There may be exceptions, such as draft messages, in which required
\[[RFC5322](#RFC5322){.xref}\] header fields are omitted in the message
literal argument to APPEND. The full implications of doing so must be
understood and carefully weighed.[¶](#section-6.3.12-3){.pilcrow}

If a flag parenthesized list is specified, the flags [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be
set in the resulting message; otherwise, the flag list of the resulting
message is set to \"empty\" by default.[¶](#section-6.3.12-4){.pilcrow}

If a date-time is specified, the internal date [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be set
in the resulting message; otherwise, the internal date of the resulting
message is set to the current date and time by
default.[¶](#section-6.3.12-5){.pilcrow}

If the append is unsuccessful for any reason, the mailbox [MUST]{.bcp14}
be restored to its state before the APPEND attempt (other than possibly
keeping the changed mailbox\'s UIDNEXT value); no partial appending is
permitted.[¶](#section-6.3.12-6){.pilcrow}

If the destination mailbox does not exist, a server [MUST]{.bcp14}
return an error and [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} automatically create the mailbox.
Unless it is certain that the destination mailbox cannot be created, the
server [MUST]{.bcp14} send the response code \"\[TRYCREATE\]\" as the
prefix of the text of the tagged NO response. This gives a hint to the
client that it can attempt a CREATE command and retry the APPEND if the
CREATE is successful.[¶](#section-6.3.12-7){.pilcrow}

On successful completion of an APPEND, the server returns an APPENDUID
response code (see [Section 7.1](#server-status-responses){.xref}),
unless otherwise specified below.[¶](#section-6.3.12-8){.pilcrow}

In the case of a mailbox that has permissions set so that the client can
APPEND to the mailbox, but not SELECT or EXAMINE it, the server [MUST
NOT]{.bcp14} send an APPENDUID response code as it would disclose
information about the mailbox.[¶](#section-6.3.12-9){.pilcrow}

In the case of a mailbox that has UIDNOTSTICKY status (see [Section
7.1](#server-status-responses){.xref}), the server [MAY]{.bcp14} omit
the APPENDUID response code as it is not
meaningful.[¶](#section-6.3.12-10){.pilcrow}

If the mailbox is currently selected, normal new message actions
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} occur. Specifically, the server [SHOULD]{.bcp14} notify
the client immediately via an untagged EXISTS response. If the server
does not do so, the client [MAY]{.bcp14} issue a NOOP command after one
or more APPEND commands.[¶](#section-6.3.12-11){.pilcrow}

If the server decides to convert (normalize) the mailbox name, it
[SHOULD]{.bcp14} return an untagged LIST with an OLDNAME extended data
item, with the OLDNAME value being the supplied mailbox name and the
name parameter being the normalized mailbox name. (See [Section
6.3.9.7](#oldname){.xref} for more
details.)[¶](#section-6.3.12-12){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.12-13){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.12-14}
``` sourcecode
  C: A003 APPEND saved-messages (\Seen) {326}
  S: + Ready for literal data
  C: Date: Mon, 7 Feb 1994 21:52:25 -0800 (PST)
  C: From: Fred Foobar <foobar@Blurdybloop.example>
  C: Subject: afternoon meeting
  C: To: mooch@owatagu.siam.edu.example
  C: Message-Id: <B27397-0100000@Blurdybloop.example>
  C: MIME-Version: 1.0
  C: Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; CHARSET=US-ASCII
  C:
  C: Hello Joe, do you think we can meet at 3:30 tomorrow?
  C:
  S: A003 OK APPEND completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.12-14){.pilcrow}
:::

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.12-15){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.12-16}
``` sourcecode
  C: A003 APPEND saved-messages (\Seen) {297+}
  C: Date: Mon, 7 Feb 1994 21:52:25 -0800 (PST)
  C: From: Fred Foobar <foobar@example.com>
  C: Subject: afternoon meeting
  C: To: mooch@example.com
  C: Message-Id: <B27397-0100000@example.com>
  C: MIME-Version: 1.0
  C: Content-Type: TEXT/PLAIN; CHARSET=US-ASCII
  C:
  C: Hello Joe, do you think we can meet at 3:30 tomorrow?
  C:
  S: A003 OK [APPENDUID 38505 3955] APPEND completed
  C: A004 COPY 2:4 meeting
  S: A004 OK [COPYUID 38505 304,319:320 3956:3958] Done
  C: A005 UID COPY 305:310 meeting
  S: A005 OK No matching messages, so nothing copied
  C: A006 COPY 2 funny
  S: A006 OK Done
  C: A007 SELECT funny
  S: * 1 EXISTS
  S: * OK [UIDVALIDITY 3857529045] Validity session-only
  S: * OK [UIDNEXT 2] Predicted next UID
  S: * NO [UIDNOTSTICKY] Non-persistent UIDs
  S: * FLAGS (\Answered \Flagged \Deleted \Seen \Draft)
  S: * OK [PERMANENTFLAGS (\Deleted \Seen)] Limited
  S: * LIST () "." funny
  S: A007 OK [READ-WRITE] SELECT completed
```

[¶](#section-6.3.12-16){.pilcrow}
:::

In this example, A003 and A004 demonstrate successful appending and
copying to a mailbox that returns the UIDs assigned to the messages.
A005 is an example in which no messages were copied; this is because in
A003, we see that message 2 had UID 304, and message 3 had UID 319;
therefore, UIDs 305 through 310 do not exist (refer to [Section
2.3.1.1](#uid-def){.xref} for further explanation). A006 is an example
of a message being copied that did not return a COPYUID; and, as
expected, A007 shows that the mail store containing that mailbox does
not support persistent UIDs.[¶](#section-6.3.12-17){.pilcrow}

Note: The APPEND command is not used for message delivery, because it
does not provide a mechanism to transfer \[[SMTP](#RFC5321){.xref}\]
envelope information.[¶](#section-6.3.12-18.1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#idle}
::: {#section-6.3.13 .section}
#### [6.3.13.](#section-6.3.13){.section-number .selfRef} [IDLE Command](#name-idle-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-idle-command}

[]{#iref-idle-command-57 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   none[¶](#section-6.3.13-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   continuation data will be requested; the client sends the
    continuation data \"DONE\" to end the
    command[¶](#section-6.3.13-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   IDLE completed after client sent
        \"DONE\"[¶](#section-6.3.13-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   failure: the server will not allow the IDLE command at this
        time[¶](#section-6.3.13-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.3.13-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Without the IDLE command, a client would need to poll the server for
changes to the selected mailbox (new mail, deletions, and flag changes).
It\'s often more desirable to have the server transmit updates to the
client in real time. This allows a user to see new mail immediately. The
IDLE command allows a client to tell the server that it\'s ready to
accept such real-time updates.[¶](#section-6.3.13-2){.pilcrow}

The IDLE command is sent from the client to the server when the client
is ready to accept unsolicited update messages. The server requests a
response to the IDLE command using the continuation (\"+\") response.
The IDLE command remains active until the client responds to the
continuation, and as long as an IDLE command is active, the server is
now free to send untagged EXISTS, EXPUNGE, FETCH, and other responses at
any time. If the server chooses to send unsolicited FETCH responses,
they [MUST]{.bcp14} include a UID FETCH
item.[¶](#section-6.3.13-3){.pilcrow}

The IDLE command is terminated by the receipt of a \"DONE\" continuation
from the client; such response satisfies the server\'s continuation
request. At that point, the server [MAY]{.bcp14} send any remaining
queued untagged responses and then [MUST]{.bcp14} immediately send the
tagged response to the IDLE command and prepare to process other
commands. As for other commands, the processing of any new command may
cause the sending of unsolicited untagged responses, subject to the
ambiguity limitations. The client [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} send a command
while the server is waiting for the DONE, since the server will not be
able to distinguish a command from a
continuation.[¶](#section-6.3.13-4){.pilcrow}

The server [MAY]{.bcp14} consider a client inactive if it has an IDLE
command running, and if such a server has an inactivity timeout, it
[MAY]{.bcp14} log the client off implicitly at the end of its timeout
period. Because of that, clients using IDLE are advised to terminate
IDLE and reissue it at least every 29 minutes to avoid being logged off.
This still allows a client to receive immediate mailbox updates even
though it need only \"poll\" at half hour
intervals.[¶](#section-6.3.13-5){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.3.13-6){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.3.13-7}
``` sourcecode
  C: A001 SELECT INBOX
  S: * FLAGS (\Deleted \Seen \Flagged)
  S: * OK [PERMANENTFLAGS (\Deleted \Seen \Flagged)] Limited
  S: * 3 EXISTS
  S: * OK [UIDVALIDITY 1]
  S: * OK [UIDNEXT 1]
  S: * LIST () "/" INBOX
  S: A001 OK [READ-WRITE] SELECT completed
  C: A002 IDLE
  S: + idling
  ...time passes; new mail arrives...
  S: * 4 EXISTS
  C: DONE
  S: A002 OK IDLE terminated
  ...another client expunges message 2 now...
  C: A003 FETCH 4 ALL
  S: * 4 FETCH (...)
  S: A003 OK FETCH completed
  C: A004 IDLE
  S: * 2 EXPUNGE
  S: * 3 EXISTS
  S: + idling
  ...time passes; another client expunges message 3...
  S: * 3 EXPUNGE
  S: * 2 EXISTS
  ...time passes; new mail arrives...
  S: * 3 EXISTS
  C: DONE
  S: A004 OK IDLE terminated
  C: A005 FETCH 3 ALL
  S: * 3 FETCH (...)
  S: A005 OK FETCH completed
  C: A006 IDLE
```

[¶](#section-6.3.13-7){.pilcrow}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.4 .section}
### [6.4.](#section-6.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Client Commands - Selected State](#name-client-commands-selected-st){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-client-commands-selected-st}

In the selected state, commands that manipulate messages in a mailbox
are permitted.[¶](#section-6.4-1){.pilcrow}

In addition to the universal commands (CAPABILITY, NOOP, and LOGOUT),
and the authenticated state commands (SELECT, EXAMINE, NAMESPACE,
CREATE, DELETE, RENAME, SUBSCRIBE, UNSUBSCRIBE, LIST, STATUS, and
APPEND), the following commands are valid in the selected state: CLOSE,
UNSELECT, EXPUNGE, SEARCH, FETCH, STORE, COPY, MOVE, and
UID.[¶](#section-6.4-2){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.1 .section}
#### [6.4.1.](#section-6.4.1){.section-number .selfRef} [CLOSE Command](#name-close-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-close-command}

[]{#iref-close-command-58 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   none[¶](#section-6.4.1-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   no specific responses for this
    command[¶](#section-6.4.1-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   close completed, now in authenticated
        state[¶](#section-6.4.1-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.4.1-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The CLOSE command permanently removes all messages that have the
\\Deleted flag set from the currently selected mailbox, and it returns
to the authenticated state from the selected state. No untagged EXPUNGE
responses are sent.[¶](#section-6.4.1-2){.pilcrow}

No messages are removed, and no error is given, if the mailbox is
selected by an EXAMINE command or is otherwise selected as
read-only.[¶](#section-6.4.1-3){.pilcrow}

Even if a mailbox is selected, a SELECT, EXAMINE, or LOGOUT command
[MAY]{.bcp14} be issued without previously issuing a CLOSE command. The
SELECT, EXAMINE, and LOGOUT commands implicitly close the currently
selected mailbox without doing an expunge. However, when many messages
are deleted, a CLOSE-LOGOUT or CLOSE-SELECT sequence is considerably
faster than an EXPUNGE-LOGOUT or EXPUNGE-SELECT because no untagged
EXPUNGE responses (which the client would probably ignore) are
sent.[¶](#section-6.4.1-4){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.4.1-5){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.1-6}
``` sourcecode
  C: A341 CLOSE
  S: A341 OK CLOSE completed
```

[¶](#section-6.4.1-6){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.4.2 .section}
#### [6.4.2.](#section-6.4.2){.section-number .selfRef} [UNSELECT Command](#name-unselect-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-unselect-command}

[]{#iref-unselect-command-59 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   none[¶](#section-6.4.2-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   no specific responses for this
    command[¶](#section-6.4.2-1.4){.pilcrow}
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   unselect completed, now in authenticated
        state[¶](#section-6.4.2-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   no mailbox selected, or argument supplied but none
        permitted[¶](#section-6.4.2-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The UNSELECT command frees a session\'s resources associated with the
selected mailbox and returns the server to the authenticated state. This
command performs the same actions as CLOSE, except that no messages are
permanently removed from the currently selected
mailbox.[¶](#section-6.4.2-2){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.4.2-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.2-4}
``` sourcecode
  C: A342 UNSELECT
  S: A342 OK Unselect completed
```

[¶](#section-6.4.2-4){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.4.3 .section}
#### [6.4.3.](#section-6.4.3){.section-number .selfRef} [EXPUNGE Command](#name-expunge-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-expunge-command}

[]{#iref-expunge-command-60 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:
:   none[¶](#section-6.4.3-1.2){.pilcrow}
:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    untagged responses:
    :   EXPUNGE[¶](#section-6.4.3-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   expunge completed[¶](#section-6.4.3-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   expunge failure: can\'t expunge (e.g., permission
        denied)[¶](#section-6.4.3-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.4.3-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The EXPUNGE command permanently removes all messages that have the
\\Deleted flag set from the currently selected mailbox. Before returning
an OK to the client, an untagged EXPUNGE response is sent for each
message that is removed.[¶](#section-6.4.3-2){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.4.3-3){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.3-4}
``` sourcecode
  C: A202 EXPUNGE
  S: * 3 EXPUNGE
  S: * 3 EXPUNGE
  S: * 5 EXPUNGE
  S: * 8 EXPUNGE
  S: A202 OK EXPUNGE completed
```

[¶](#section-6.4.3-4){.pilcrow}
:::

Note: In this example, messages 3, 4, 7, and 11 had the \\Deleted flag
set. See the description of the EXPUNGE response ([Section
7.5.1](#expunge-response){.xref}) for further
explanation.[¶](#section-6.4.3-5){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#section-6.4.4 .section}
#### [6.4.4.](#section-6.4.4){.section-number .selfRef} [SEARCH Command](#name-search-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-search-command}

[]{#iref-search-command-61 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:

:   [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} result
    specifier[¶](#section-6.4.4-1.2.1){.pilcrow}

    [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} \[[CHARSET](#RFC2978){.xref}\]
    specification[¶](#section-6.4.4-1.2.2){.pilcrow}

    searching criteria (one or more)[¶](#section-6.4.4-1.2.3){.pilcrow}

:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} untagged response:
    :   ESEARCH[¶](#section-6.4.4-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   search completed[¶](#section-6.4.4-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   search error: can\'t search that \[[CHARSET](#RFC2978){.xref}\]
        or criteria[¶](#section-6.4.4-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.4.4-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The SEARCH command searches the mailbox for messages that match the
given searching criteria.[¶](#section-6.4.4-2){.pilcrow}

The SEARCH command may contain result options. Result options control
what kind of information is returned about messages matching the search
criteria in an untagged ESEARCH response. If no result option is
specified or empty list of options is specified as \"()\", ALL is
assumed (see below). The order of individual options is arbitrary.
Individual options may contain parameters enclosed in parentheses.
(However, if an option has a mandatory parameter, which can always be
represented as a number or a sequence-set, the option parameter does not
need the enclosing parentheses. See \"Formal Syntax\" ([Section
9](#IMAP-ABNF){.xref}) for more details.) If an option has parameters,
they consist of atoms and/or strings and/or lists in a specific order.
Any options not defined by extensions that the server supports
[MUST]{.bcp14} be rejected with a BAD
response.[¶](#section-6.4.4-3){.pilcrow}

Note that IMAP4rev1 used SEARCH responses \[[RFC3501](#RFC3501){.xref}\]
instead of ESEARCH responses. Clients that support only IMAP4rev2
[MUST]{.bcp14} ignore SEARCH responses.[¶](#section-6.4.4-4){.pilcrow}

This document specifies the following result
options:[¶](#section-6.4.4-5){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

MIN

:   []{#iref-min-search-result-option-62 .iref} Return the lowest
    message number/UID that satisfies the SEARCH
    criteria.[¶](#section-6.4.4-6.2.1){.pilcrow}

    If the SEARCH results in no matches, the server [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
    include the MIN result option in the ESEARCH response; however, it
    still [MUST]{.bcp14} send the ESEARCH
    response.[¶](#section-6.4.4-6.2.2){.pilcrow}

:   

MAX

:   []{#iref-max-search-result-option-63 .iref} Return the highest
    message number/UID that satisfies the SEARCH
    criteria.[¶](#section-6.4.4-6.4.1){.pilcrow}

    If the SEARCH results in no matches, the server [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
    include the MAX result option in the ESEARCH response; however, it
    still [MUST]{.bcp14} send the ESEARCH
    response.[¶](#section-6.4.4-6.4.2){.pilcrow}

:   

ALL

:   []{#iref-all-search-result-option-64 .iref} Return all message
    numbers/UIDs that satisfy the SEARCH criteria using the sequence-set
    syntax. Note that the client [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} assume that
    messages/UIDs will be listed in any particular
    order.[¶](#section-6.4.4-6.6.1){.pilcrow}

    If the SEARCH results in no matches, the server [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
    include the ALL result option in the ESEARCH response; however, it
    still [MUST]{.bcp14} send the ESEARCH
    response.[¶](#section-6.4.4-6.6.2){.pilcrow}

:   

COUNT
:   []{#iref-count-search-result-option- .iref} Return the number of
    messages that satisfy the SEARCH criteria. This result option
    [MUST]{.bcp14} always be included in the ESEARCH
    response.[¶](#section-6.4.4-6.8){.pilcrow}
:   

SAVE

:   []{#iref-save-search-result-option-6 .iref} This option tells the
    server to remember the result of the SEARCH or UID SEARCH command
    (as well as any command based on SEARCH, e.g., SORT and THREAD
    \[[RFC5256](#RFC5256){.xref}\]) and store it in an internal variable
    that we will reference as the \"search result variable\". The client
    can use the \"\$\" marker to reference the content of this internal
    variable. The \"\$\" marker can be used instead of message sequence
    or UID sequence in order to indicate that the server should
    substitute it with the list of messages from the search result
    variable. Thus, the client can use the result of the latest
    remembered SEARCH command as a parameter to another command. See
    [Section 6.4.4.1](#search-save){.xref} for details on how the value
    of the search result variable is determined, how it is affected by
    other commands executed, and how the SAVE return option interacts
    with other return options.[¶](#section-6.4.4-6.10.1){.pilcrow}

    In absence of any other SEARCH result option, the SAVE result option
    also suppresses any ESEARCH response that would have been otherwise
    returned by the SEARCH command.[¶](#section-6.4.4-6.10.2){.pilcrow}

:   

Note: future extensions to this document can allow servers to return
multiple ESEARCH responses for a single extended SEARCH command.
However, all options specified above [MUST]{.bcp14} result in a single
ESEARCH response if used by themselves or in combination. This guarantee
simplifies processing in IMAP4rev2 clients. Future SEARCH extensions
that relax this restriction will have to describe how results from
multiple ESEARCH responses are to be
combined.[¶](#section-6.4.4-7){.pilcrow}

Searching criteria consist of one or more search
keys.[¶](#section-6.4.4-8){.pilcrow}

When multiple keys are specified, the result is the intersection (AND
function) of all the messages that match those keys. For example, the
criteria DELETED FROM \"SMITH\" SINCE 1-Feb-1994 refers to all deleted
messages from Smith with INTERNALDATE greater than February 1, 1994. A
search key can also be a parenthesized list of one or more search keys
(e.g., for use with the OR and NOT keys).[¶](#section-6.4.4-9){.pilcrow}

Server implementations [MAY]{.bcp14} exclude
\[[MIME-IMB](#RFC2045){.xref}\] body parts with terminal content media
types other than TEXT and MESSAGE from consideration in SEARCH
matching.[¶](#section-6.4.4-10){.pilcrow}

The [OPTIONAL]{.bcp14} \[[CHARSET](#RFC2978){.xref}\] specification
consists of the word \"CHARSET\" followed by the name of a character set
from the registry \[[CHARSET-REG](#CHARSET-REG){.xref}\]. It indicates
the \[[CHARSET](#RFC2978){.xref}\] of the strings that appear in the
search criteria. \[[MIME-IMB](#RFC2045){.xref}\] content transfer
encodings and \[[MIME-HDRS](#RFC2047){.xref}\] strings in
\[[RFC5322](#RFC5322){.xref}\]/\[[MIME-IMB](#RFC2045){.xref}\] headers
[MUST]{.bcp14} be decoded before comparing text. Servers [MUST]{.bcp14}
support US-ASCII and UTF-8 charsets; other CHARSETs [MAY]{.bcp14} be
supported. Clients [SHOULD]{.bcp14} use UTF-8. Note that if CHARSET is
not provided, IMAP4rev2 servers [MUST]{.bcp14} assume UTF-8, so
selecting CHARSET UTF-8 is redundant. It is permitted for improved
compatibility with existing IMAP4rev1
clients.[¶](#section-6.4.4-11){.pilcrow}

If the server does not support the specified
\[[CHARSET](#RFC2978){.xref}\], it [MUST]{.bcp14} return a tagged NO
response (not a BAD). This response [SHOULD]{.bcp14} contain the
BADCHARSET response code, which [MAY]{.bcp14} list the CHARSETs
supported by the server.[¶](#section-6.4.4-12){.pilcrow}

In all search keys that use strings, and unless otherwise specified, a
message matches the key if the string is a substring of the associated
text. The matching [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be case insensitive for characters
within the ASCII range. Consider using \[[IMAP-I18N](#RFC5255){.xref}\]
for language-sensitive, case-insensitive searching. Note that the empty
string is a substring; this is useful when performing a HEADER search in
order to test for a header field presence in the
message.[¶](#section-6.4.4-13){.pilcrow}

The defined search keys are as follows. Refer to \"Formal Syntax\"
([Section 9](#IMAP-ABNF){.xref}) for the precise syntactic definitions
of the arguments.[¶](#section-6.4.4-14){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

\<sequence set>
:   Messages with message sequence numbers corresponding to the
    specified message sequence number
    set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.2){.pilcrow}
:   

ALL
:   []{#iref-all-search-key-67 .iref} All messages in the mailbox; the
    default initial key for ANDing.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.4){.pilcrow}
:   

ANSWERED
:   []{#iref-answered-search-key-68 .iref} Messages with the \\Answered
    flag set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.6){.pilcrow}
:   

BCC \<string>
:   []{#iref-bcc-string-search-key-69 .iref} Messages that contain the
    specified string in the envelope structure\'s Blind Carbon Copy
    (BCC) field.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.8){.pilcrow}
:   

BEFORE \<date>
:   []{#iref-before-date-search-key-70 .iref} Messages whose internal
    date (disregarding time and timezone) is earlier than the specified
    date.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.10){.pilcrow}
:   

BODY \<string>
:   []{#iref-body-string-search-key-71 .iref} Messages that contain the
    specified string in the body of the message. Unlike TEXT (see
    below), this doesn\'t match any header fields. Servers are allowed
    to implement flexible matching for this search key, for example, by
    matching \"swim\" to both \"swam\" and \"swum\" in English language
    text or only performing full word matching (where \"swim\" will not
    match \"swimming\").[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.12){.pilcrow}
:   

CC \<string>
:   []{#iref-cc-string-search-key-72 .iref} Messages that contain the
    specified string in the envelope structure\'s CC
    field.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.14){.pilcrow}
:   

DELETED
:   []{#iref-deleted-search-key-73 .iref} Messages with the \\Deleted
    flag set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.16){.pilcrow}
:   

DRAFT
:   []{#iref-draft-search-key-74 .iref} Messages with the \\Draft flag
    set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.18){.pilcrow}
:   

FLAGGED
:   []{#iref-flagged-search-key-75 .iref} Messages with the \\Flagged
    flag set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.20){.pilcrow}
:   

FROM \<string>
:   []{#iref-from-string-search-key-76 .iref} Messages that contain the
    specified string in the envelope structure\'s FROM
    field.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.22){.pilcrow}
:   

HEADER \<field-name> \<string>
:   []{#iref-header-field-name-string-se .iref} Messages that have a
    header field with the specified field-name (as defined in
    \[[RFC5322](#RFC5322){.xref}\]) and that contain the specified
    string in the text of the header field (what comes after the colon).
    If the string to search is zero-length, this matches all messages
    that have a header field with the specified field-name regardless of
    the contents. Servers should use a substring search for this SEARCH
    item, as clients can use it for automatic processing not initiated
    by end users. For example, this can be used when searching for
    Message-ID or Content-Type header field values that need to be exact
    or for searches in header fields that the IMAP server might not know
    anything about.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.24){.pilcrow}
:   

KEYWORD \<flag>
:   []{#iref-keyword-flag-search-key-78 .iref} Messages with the
    specified keyword flag set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.26){.pilcrow}
:   

LARGER \<n>
:   []{#iref-larger-n-search-key-79 .iref} Messages with an RFC822.SIZE
    larger than the specified number of
    octets.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.28){.pilcrow}
:   

NOT \<search-key>
:   []{#iref-not-search-key-search-key-8 .iref} Messages that do not
    match the specified search key.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.30){.pilcrow}
:   

ON \<date>
:   []{#iref-on-date-search-key-81 .iref} Messages whose internal date
    (disregarding time and timezone) is within the specified
    date.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.32){.pilcrow}
:   

OR \<search-key1> \<search-key2>
:   []{#iref-or-search-key1-search-key2- .iref} Messages that match
    either search key.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.34){.pilcrow}
:   

SEEN
:   []{#iref-seen-search-key-83 .iref} Messages that have the \\Seen
    flag set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.36){.pilcrow}
:   

SENTBEFORE \<date>
:   []{#iref-sentbefore-date-search-key- .iref} Messages whose
    \[[RFC5322](#RFC5322){.xref}\] Date: header field (disregarding time
    and timezone) is earlier than the specified
    date.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.38){.pilcrow}
:   

SENTON \<date>
:   []{#iref-senton-date-search-key-85 .iref} Messages whose
    \[[RFC5322](#RFC5322){.xref}\] Date: header field (disregarding time
    and timezone) is within the specified
    date.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.40){.pilcrow}
:   

SENTSINCE \<date>
:   []{#iref-sentsince-date-search-key-8 .iref} Messages whose
    \[[RFC5322](#RFC5322){.xref}\] Date: header field (disregarding time
    and timezone) is within or later than the specified
    date.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.42){.pilcrow}
:   

SINCE \<date>
:   []{#iref-since-date-search-key-87 .iref} Messages whose internal
    date (disregarding time and timezone) is within or later than the
    specified date.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.44){.pilcrow}
:   

SMALLER \<n>
:   []{#iref-smaller-n-search-key-88 .iref} Messages with an RFC822.SIZE
    smaller than the specified number of
    octets.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.46){.pilcrow}
:   

SUBJECT \<string>
:   []{#iref-subject-string-search-key-8 .iref} Messages that contain
    the specified string in the envelope structure\'s SUBJECT
    field.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.48){.pilcrow}
:   

TEXT \<string>
:   []{#iref-text-string-search-key-90 .iref} Messages that contain the
    specified string in the header (including MIME header fields) or
    body of the message. Servers are allowed to implement flexible
    matching for this search key, for example, matching \"swim\" to both
    \"swam\" and \"swum\" in English language text or only performing
    full-word matching (where \"swim\" will not match
    \"swimming\").[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.50){.pilcrow}
:   

TO \<string>
:   []{#iref-to-string-search-key-91 .iref} Messages that contain the
    specified string in the envelope structure\'s TO
    field.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.52){.pilcrow}
:   

UID \<sequence set>
:   []{#iref-uid-sequence-set-search-key .iref} Messages with unique
    identifiers corresponding to the specified unique identifier set.
    Sequence-set ranges are
    permitted.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.54){.pilcrow}
:   

UNANSWERED
:   []{#iref-unanswered-search-key-93 .iref} Messages that do not have
    the \\Answered flag set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.56){.pilcrow}
:   

UNDELETED
:   []{#iref-undeleted-search-key-94 .iref} Messages that do not have
    the \\Deleted flag set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.58){.pilcrow}
:   

UNDRAFT
:   []{#iref-undraft-search-key-95 .iref} Messages that do not have the
    \\Draft flag set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.60){.pilcrow}
:   

UNFLAGGED
:   []{#iref-unflagged-search-key-96 .iref} Messages that do not have
    the \\Flagged flag set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.62){.pilcrow}
:   

UNKEYWORD \<flag>
:   []{#iref-unkeyword-flag-search-key-9 .iref} Messages that do not
    have the specified keyword flag
    set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.64){.pilcrow}
:   

UNSEEN
:   []{#iref-unseen-search-key-98 .iref} Messages that do not have the
    \\Seen flag set.[¶](#section-6.4.4-15.66){.pilcrow}
:   

Example:[¶](#section-6.4.4-16){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.4-17}
``` sourcecode
  C: A282 SEARCH RETURN (MIN COUNT) FLAGGED
      SINCE 1-Feb-1994 NOT FROM "Smith"
  S: * ESEARCH (TAG "A282") MIN 2 COUNT 3
  S: A282 OK SEARCH completed
```

[¶](#section-6.4.4-17){.pilcrow}
:::

Example:[¶](#section-6.4.4-18){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.4-19}
``` sourcecode
  C: A283 SEARCH RETURN () FLAGGED
      SINCE 1-Feb-1994 NOT FROM "Smith"
  S: * ESEARCH (TAG "A283") ALL 2,10:11
  S: A283 OK SEARCH completed
```

[¶](#section-6.4.4-19){.pilcrow}
:::

Example:[¶](#section-6.4.4-20){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.4-21}
``` sourcecode
  C: A284 SEARCH TEXT "string not in mailbox"
  S: * ESEARCH (TAG "A284")
  S: A284 OK SEARCH completed
  C: A285 SEARCH CHARSET UTF-8 TEXT {12}
  S: + Ready for literal text
  C: отпуск
  S: * ESEARCH (TAG "A285") ALL 43
  S: A285 OK SEARCH completed
```

[¶](#section-6.4.4-21){.pilcrow}
:::

The following example demonstrates finding the first unseen message in
the mailbox:[¶](#section-6.4.4-23){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.4.4-24){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.4-25}
``` sourcecode
  C: A284 SEARCH RETURN (MIN) UNSEEN
  S: * ESEARCH (TAG "A284") MIN 4
  S: A284 OK SEARCH completed
```

[¶](#section-6.4.4-25){.pilcrow}
:::

The following example demonstrates that if the ESEARCH UID indicator is
present, all data in the ESEARCH response is referring to UIDs; for
example, the MIN result specifier will be followed by a
UID.[¶](#section-6.4.4-26){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.4.4-27){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.4-28}
``` sourcecode
  C: A285 UID SEARCH RETURN (MIN MAX) 1:5000
  S: * ESEARCH (TAG "A285") UID MIN 7 MAX 3800
  S: A285 OK SEARCH completed
```

[¶](#section-6.4.4-28){.pilcrow}
:::

The following example demonstrates returning the number of deleted
messages:[¶](#section-6.4.4-29){.pilcrow}

Example:[¶](#section-6.4.4-30){.pilcrow}

::: {#section-6.4.4-31}
``` sourcecode
  C: A286 SEARCH RETURN (COUNT) DELETED
  S: * ESEARCH (TAG "A286") COUNT 15
  S: A286 OK SEARCH completed
```

[¶](#section-6.4.4-31){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#search-save}
::: {#section-6.4.4.1 .section}
##### [6.4.4.1.](#section-6.4.4.1){.section-number .selfRef} [SAVE Result Option and SEARCH Result Variable](#name-save-result-option-and-sear){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-save-result-option-and-sear}

Upon successful completion of a SELECT or an EXAMINE command (after the
tagged OK response), the current search result variable is reset to the
empty sequence.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-1){.pilcrow}

A successful SEARCH command with the SAVE result option sets the value
of the search result variable to the list of messages found in the
SEARCH command. For example, if no messages were found, the search
result variable will contain the empty
sequence.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-2){.pilcrow}

Any of the following SEARCH commands [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} change the
search result variable:[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-3){.pilcrow}

-   [a SEARCH command that caused the server to return the BAD tagged
    response,[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-4.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.4.4.1-4.1}
-   [a SEARCH command with no SAVE result option that caused the server
    to return NO tagged response,
    and[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-4.2){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.4.4.1-4.2}
-   [a successful SEARCH command with no SAVE result
    option.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-4.3){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.4.4.1-4.3}

A SEARCH command with the SAVE result option that caused the server to
return the NO tagged response sets the value of the search result
variable to the empty sequence.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-5){.pilcrow}

When a message listed in the search result variable is EXPUNGEd, it is
automatically removed from the list. Implementors are reminded that if
the server stores the list as a list of message numbers, it
[MUST]{.bcp14} automatically adjust them when notifying the client about
expunged messages, as described in [Section
7.5.1](#expunge-response){.xref}.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-6){.pilcrow}

If the server decides to send a new UIDVALIDITY value while the mailbox
is opened, it causes the resetting of the search variable to the empty
sequence.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-7){.pilcrow}

Note that even if the \"\$\" marker contains the empty sequence of
messages, it must be treated by all commands accepting message sets as
parameters as a valid, but non-matching, list of messages. For example,
the \"FETCH \$\" command would return a tagged OK response and no FETCH
responses. See also Example 5 in [Section
6.4.4.4](#search-save-examples){.xref}.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-8){.pilcrow}

The SAVE result option doesn\'t change whether the server would return
items corresponding to MIN, MAX, ALL, or COUNT result
options.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-9){.pilcrow}

When the SAVE result option is combined with the MIN or MAX result
option, and both ALL and COUNT result options are absent, the
corresponding MIN/MAX is returned (if the search result is not empty),
but the \"\$\" marker would contain a single message as returned in the
MIN/MAX return item.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-10){.pilcrow}

If the SAVE result option is combined with both MIN and MAX result
options, and both ALL and COUNT result options are absent, the \"\$\"
marker would contain zero messages, one message, or two messages as
returned in the MIN/MAX return items.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-11){.pilcrow}

If the SAVE result option is combined with the ALL and/or COUNT result
option(s), the \"\$\" marker would always contain all messages found by
the SEARCH or UID SEARCH command.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-12){.pilcrow}

The following table summarizes the additional requirement on ESEARCH
server implementations described in this
section.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-13){.pilcrow}

  Combination of Result Option   \"\$\" Marker Value
  ------------------------------ ---------------------
  SAVE MIN                       MIN
  SAVE MAX                       MAX
  SAVE MIN MAX                   MIN & MAX
  SAVE \* \[m\]                  all found messages

  : [Table 4](#table-4){.selfRef}

where \'\*\' means \"ALL\" and/or \"COUNT\", and \'\[m\]\' means
optional \"MIN\" and/or \"MAX\"[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-15){.pilcrow}

Implementation note: server implementors should note that \"\$\" can
reference IMAP message sequences or UID sequences, depending on the
context where it is used. For example, the \"\$\" marker can be set as a
result of a SEARCH (SAVE) command and used as a parameter to a UID FETCH
command (which accepts a UID sequence, not a message sequence), or the
\"\$\" marker can be set as a result of a UID SEARCH (SAVE) command and
used as a parameter to a FETCH command (which accepts a message
sequence, not a UID sequence). Server implementations need to
automatically map the \"\$\" marker value to message numbers or UIDs,
depending on the context where the \"\$\" marker is
used.[¶](#section-6.4.4.1-16){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#search-save-pipelining}
::: {#section-6.4.4.2 .section}
##### [6.4.4.2.](#section-6.4.4.2){.section-number .selfRef} [Multiple Commands in Progress](#name-multiple-commands-in-progres){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-multiple-commands-in-progres}

Use of a SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) command followed by a command using the
\"\$\" marker creates direct dependency between the two commands. As
directed by [Section 5.5](#pipelining){.xref}, a server [MUST]{.bcp14}
execute the two commands in the order they were
received.[¶](#section-6.4.4.2-1){.pilcrow}

A client [MAY]{.bcp14} pipeline a SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) command with one
or more commands using the \"\$\" marker, as long as this doesn\'t
create an ambiguity, as described in [Section 5.5](#pipelining){.xref}.
Examples 7-9 in [Section 6.4.4.4](#search-save-examples){.xref} explain
this in more details.[¶](#section-6.4.4.2-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#section-6.4.4.3 .section}
##### [6.4.4.3.](#section-6.4.4.3){.section-number .selfRef} [Refusing to Save Search Results](#name-refusing-to-save-search-res){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-refusing-to-save-search-res}

In some cases, the server [MAY]{.bcp14} refuse to save a SEARCH (SAVE)
result, for example, if an internal limit on the number of saved results
is reached. In this case, the server [MUST]{.bcp14} return a tagged NO
response containing the NOTSAVED response code and set the search result
variable to the empty sequence, as described in [Section
6.4.4.1](#search-save){.xref}.[¶](#section-6.4.4.3-1){.pilcrow}
:::

::: {#search-save-examples}
::: {#section-6.4.4.4 .section}
##### [6.4.4.4.](#section-6.4.4.4){.section-number .selfRef} [Examples Showing Use of the SAVE Result Option](#name-examples-showing-use-of-the){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-examples-showing-use-of-the}

Only in this section: explanatory comments in examples that start with
// are not part of the protocol.[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-1){.pilcrow}

1.  ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.1}
    The following example demonstrates how the client can use the result
    of a SEARCH command to FETCH headers of interesting
    messages:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.1.1){.pilcrow}

    Example 1:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.1.2){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.1.3}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A282 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) FLAGGED SINCE 1-Feb-1994
          NOT FROM "Smith"
      S: A282 OK SEARCH completed, result saved
      C: A283 FETCH $ (UID INTERNALDATE FLAGS BODY.PEEK[HEADER])
      S: * 2 FETCH (UID 14 ...
      S: * 84 FETCH (UID 100 ...
      S: * 882 FETCH (UID 1115 ...
      S: A283 OK completed
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.1.3){.pilcrow}
    :::

    The client can also pipeline the two
    commands:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.1.4){.pilcrow}

    Example 2:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.1.5){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.1.6}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A282 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) FLAGGED SINCE 1-Feb-1994
          NOT FROM "Smith"
      C: A283 FETCH $ (UID INTERNALDATE FLAGS BODY.PEEK[HEADER])
      S: A282 OK SEARCH completed
      S: * 2 FETCH (UID 14 ...
      S: * 84 FETCH (UID 100 ...
      S: * 882 FETCH (UID 1115 ...
      S: A283 OK completed
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

2.  ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.2}
    The following example demonstrates that the result of one SEARCH
    command can be used as input to another SEARCH
    command:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.2.1){.pilcrow}

    Example 3:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.2.2){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.2.3}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A300 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) SINCE 1-Jan-2004
          NOT FROM "Smith"
      S: A300 OK SEARCH completed
      C: A301 UID SEARCH UID $ SMALLER 4096
      S: * ESEARCH (TAG "A301") UID ALL 17,900,901
      S: A301 OK completed
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.2.3){.pilcrow}
    :::

    Note that the second command in Example 3 can be replaced
    with:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.2.4){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.2.5}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: A301 UID SEARCH $ SMALLER 4096
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.2.5){.pilcrow}
    :::

    and the result of the command would be the
    same.[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.2.6){.pilcrow}
    :::

3.  ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.3}
    The following example shows that the \"\$\" marker can be combined
    with other message numbers using the OR SEARCH
    criterion.[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.3.1){.pilcrow}

    Example 4:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.3.2){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.3.3}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: P282 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) SINCE 1-Feb-1994
          NOT FROM "Smith"
      S: P282 OK SEARCH completed
      C: P283 SEARCH CHARSET UTF-8 (OR $ 1,3000:3021) TEXT {8+}
      C: мать
      S: * ESEARCH (TAG "P283") ALL 882,1102,3003,3005:3006
      S: P283 OK completed
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.3.3){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::

4.  ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.4}
    The following example demonstrates that a failed SEARCH sets the
    search result variable to the empty list. The server doesn\'t
    implement the KOI8-R charset.[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.4.1){.pilcrow}

    Example 5:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.4.2){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.4.3}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: B282 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) SINCE 1-Feb-1994
          NOT FROM "Smith"
      S: B282 OK SEARCH completed
      C: B283 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) CHARSET KOI8-R
          (OR $ 1,3000:3021) TEXT {4}
      C: XXXX
      S: B283 NO [BADCHARSET UTF-8] KOI8-R is not supported
     //After this command, the saved result variable contains
     //no messages.  A client that wants to reissue the B283
     //SEARCH command with another CHARSET would have to reissue
     //the B282 command as well.  One possible workaround for
     //this is to include the desired CHARSET parameter
     //in the earliest SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) command in a
     //sequence of related SEARCH commands, to cause
     //the earliest SEARCH in the sequence to fail.
     //A better approach might be to always use CHARSET UTF-8
     //instead.
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.4.3){.pilcrow}
    :::

    Note: Since this document format is restricted to 7-bit ASCII text,
    it is not possible to show actual KOI8-R data. The \"XXXX\" is a
    placeholder for what would be 4 octets of 8-bit data in an actual
    transaction.[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.4.4){.pilcrow}
    :::

5.  ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.5}
    The following example demonstrates that it is not an error to use
    the \"\$\" marker when it contains no
    messages.[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.1){.pilcrow}

    Example 6:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.2){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.3}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: E282 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) SINCE 28-Oct-2006
          NOT FROM "Eric"
      C: E283 COPY $ "Other Messages"
     //The "$" contains no messages
      S: E282 OK SEARCH completed
      S: E283 OK COPY completed, nothing copied
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.3){.pilcrow}
    :::

    Example 7:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.4){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.5}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: F282 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) KEYWORD $Junk
      C: F283 COPY $ "Junk"
      C: F284 STORE $ +FLAGS.Silent (\Deleted)
      S: F282 OK SEARCH completed
      S: F283 OK COPY completed
      S: F284 OK STORE completed
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.5){.pilcrow}
    :::

    Example 8:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.6){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.7}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: G282 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) KEYWORD $Junk
      C: G283 SEARCH RETURN (ALL) SINCE 28-Oct-2006
          FROM "Eric"
     // The server can execute the two SEARCH commands
     // in any order, as they don't have any dependency.
     // For example, it may return:
      S: * ESEARCH (TAG "G283") ALL 3:15,27,29:103
      S: G283 OK SEARCH completed
      S: G282 OK SEARCH completed
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.7){.pilcrow}
    :::

    The following example demonstrates that the result of the second
    SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) always overrides the result of the
    first.[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.8){.pilcrow}

    Example 9:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.9){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.10}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: H282 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) KEYWORD $Junk
      C: H283 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE) SINCE 28-Oct-2006
          FROM "Eric"
      S: H282 OK SEARCH completed
      S: H283 OK SEARCH completed
     // At this point "$" would contain results of H283
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.10){.pilcrow}
    :::

    The following example demonstrates behavioral difference for
    different combinations of ESEARCH result
    options.[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.11){.pilcrow}

    Example 10:[¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.12){.pilcrow}

    ::: {#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.13}
    ``` sourcecode
      C: C282 SEARCH RETURN (ALL) SINCE 12-Feb-2006
          NOT FROM "Smith"
      S: * ESEARCH (TAG "C283") ALL 2,10:15,21
    //$ value hasn't changed
      S: C282 OK SEARCH completed

      C: C283 SEARCH RETURN (ALL SAVE) SINCE 12-Feb-2006
          NOT FROM "Smith"
      S: * ESEARCH (TAG "C283") ALL 2,10:15,21
    //$ value is 2,10:15,21
      S: C283 OK SEARCH completed

      C: C284 SEARCH RETURN (SAVE MIN) SINCE 12-Feb-2006
          NOT FROM "Smith"
      S: * ESEARCH (TAG "C284") MIN 2
    //$ value is 2
      S: C284 OK SEARCH completed

      C: C285 SEARCH RETURN (MAX SAVE MIN) SINCE
          12-Feb-2006 NOT FROM "Smith"
      S: * ESEARCH (TAG "C285") MIN 2 MAX 21
    //$ value is 2,21
      S: C285 OK SEARCH completed

      C: C286 SEARCH RETURN (MAX SAVE MIN COUNT)
          SINCE 12-Feb-2006 NOT FROM "Smith"
      S: * ESEARCH (TAG "C286") MIN 2 MAX 21 COUNT 8
    //$ value is 2,10:15,21
      S: C286 OK SEARCH completed

      C: C286 SEARCH RETURN (ALL SAVE MIN) SINCE
          12-Feb-2006 NOT FROM "Smith"
      S: * ESEARCH (TAG "C286") MIN 2 ALL 2,10:15,21
    //$ value is 2,10:15,21
      S: C286 OK SEARCH completed
    ```

    [¶](#section-6.4.4.4-2.5.13){.pilcrow}
    :::
    :::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#fetch-command}
::: {#section-6.4.5 .section}
#### [6.4.5.](#section-6.4.5){.section-number .selfRef} [FETCH Command](#name-fetch-command){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-fetch-command}

[]{#iref-fetch-command-99 .iref} []{.break}

Arguments:

:   sequence set[¶](#section-6.4.5-1.2.1){.pilcrow}

    message data item names or macro[¶](#section-6.4.5-1.2.2){.pilcrow}

:   

Responses:
:   []{.break}

    untagged responses:
    :   FETCH[¶](#section-6.4.5-1.4.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

Result:
:   []{.break}

    OK -
    :   fetch completed[¶](#section-6.4.5-1.6.1.2){.pilcrow}
    :   

    NO -
    :   fetch error: can\'t fetch that
        data[¶](#section-6.4.5-1.6.1.4){.pilcrow}
    :   

    BAD -
    :   command unknown or arguments
        invalid[¶](#section-6.4.5-1.6.1.6){.pilcrow}
    :   
:   

The FETCH command retrieves data associated with a message in the
mailbox. The data items to be fetched can be either a single atom or a
parenthesized list.[¶](#section-6.4.5-2){.pilcrow}

Most data items, identified in the formal syntax ([Section
9](#IMAP-ABNF){.xref}) under the msg-att-static rule, are static and
[MUST NOT]{.bcp14} change for any particular message. Other data items,
identified in the formal syntax under the msg-att-dynamic rule,
[MAY]{.bcp14} change either as a result of a STORE command or due to
external events.[¶](#section-6.4.5-3){.pilcrow}

-   [For example, if a client receives an ENVELOPE for a message when it
    already knows the envelope, it can safely ignore the newly
    transmitted
    envelope.[¶](#section-6.4.5-4.1){.pilcrow}]{#section-6.4.5-4.1}

There are three macros that specify commonly used sets of data items and
can be used instead of data items. A macro must be used by itself and
not in conjunction with other macros or data
items.[¶](#section-6.4.5-5){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

ALL
:   []{#iref-all-fetch-item-100 .iref} Macro equivalent to: (FLAGS
    INTERNALDATE RFC822.SIZE ENVELOPE)[¶](#section-6.4.5-6.2){.pilcrow}
:   

FAST
:   []{#iref-fast-fetch-item-101 .iref} Macro equivalent to: (FLAGS
    INTERNALDATE RFC822.SIZE)[¶](#section-6.4.5-6.4){.pilcrow}
:   

FULL
:   []{#iref-full-fetch-item-102 .iref} Macro equivalent to: (FLAGS
    INTERNALDATE RFC822.SIZE ENVELOPE
    BODY)[¶](#section-6.4.5-6.6){.pilcrow}
:   

Several data items reference \"section\" or \"section-binary\". See
[Section 6.4.5.1](#fetch-section){.xref} for their detailed
definition.[¶](#section-6.4.5-7){.pilcrow}

The currently defined data items that can be fetched
are:[¶](#section-6.4.5-8){.pilcrow}

[]{.break}

BINARY\[\<section-binary>\]\<\<partial>\>

:   []{#iref-binarysection-binarypartial .iref} Requests that the
    specified section be transmitted after performing decoding of the
    section\'s
    Content-Transfer-Encoding.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.2.1){.pilcrow}

    The \<partial> argument, if present, requests that a subset of the
    data be returned. The semantics of a partial FETCH BINARY command
    are the same as for a partial FETCH BODY command, with the exception
    that the \<partial> arguments refer to the DECODED section
    data.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.2.2){.pilcrow}

    Note that this data item can only be requested for leaf body parts:
    those that have media types other than multipart/\*, message/rfc822,
    or message/global.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.2.3){.pilcrow}

:   

BINARY.PEEK\[\<section-binary>\]\<\<partial>\>
:   []{#iref-binarypeeksection-binarypar .iref} An alternate form of
    BINARY\[\<section-binary>\] that does not implicitly set the \\Seen
    flag.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.4){.pilcrow}
:   

BINARY.SIZE\[\<section-binary>\]

:   []{#iref-binarysizesection-binary-fe .iref} Requests the decoded
    size of the section (i.e., the size to expect in response to the
    corresponding FETCH BINARY
    request).[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.6.1){.pilcrow}

    Note: client authors are cautioned that this might be an expensive
    operation for some server implementations. Needlessly issuing this
    request could result in degraded performance due to servers having
    to calculate the value every time the request is
    issued.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.6.2){.pilcrow}

    Note that this data item can only be requested for leaf body parts:
    those that have media types other than multipart/\*, message/rfc822,
    or message/global.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.6.3){.pilcrow}

:   

BODY
:   []{#iref-body-fetch-item-106 .iref} Non-extensible form of
    BODYSTRUCTURE.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.8){.pilcrow}
:   

BODY\[\<section>\]\<\<partial>\>

:   []{#iref-bodysectionpartial-fetch-it .iref} The text of a particular
    body section. If BODY\[\] is specified (the section specification is
    omitted), the FETCH is requesting the \[[RFC5322](#RFC5322){.xref}\]
    expression of the entire
    message.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.10.1){.pilcrow}

    It is possible to fetch a substring of the designated text. This is
    done by appending an open angle bracket (\"\<\"), the octet position
    of the first desired octet, a period, the maximum number of octets
    desired, and a close angle bracket (\"\>\") to the part specifier.
    If the starting octet is beyond the end of the text, an empty string
    is returned.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.10.2){.pilcrow}

    Any partial fetch that attempts to read beyond the end of the text
    is truncated as appropriate. A partial fetch that starts at octet 0
    is returned as a partial fetch, even if this truncation
    happened.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.10.3){.pilcrow}

    Note: This means that BODY\[\]\<0.2048> of a 1500-octet message will
    return BODY\[\]\<0> with a literal of size 1500, not
    BODY\[\].[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.10.4){.pilcrow}

    Note: A substring fetch of a HEADER.FIELDS or HEADER.FIELDS.NOT part
    specifier is calculated after subsetting the
    header.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.10.5){.pilcrow}

    The \\Seen flag is implicitly set; if this causes the flags to
    change, they [SHOULD]{.bcp14} be included as part of the FETCH
    responses.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.10.6){.pilcrow}

:   

BODY.PEEK\[\<section>\]\<\<partial>\>
:   []{#iref-bodypeeksectionpartial-fetc .iref} An alternate form of
    BODY\[\<section>\] that does not implicitly set the \\Seen
    flag.[¶](#section-6.4.5-9.12){.pilcrow}
:   

BODYSTRUCTURE
