::: {#IMAP4rev1-compat}
::: {#appendix-A .section}
## [Appendix A.](#appendix-A){.section-number .selfRef} [Backward Compatibility with IMAP4rev1](#name-backward-compatibility-with){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-backward-compatibility-with}

An implementation that wants to remain compatible with IMAP4rev1 can
advertise both IMAP4rev1 and IMAP4rev2 in its CAPABILITY response /
response code. (Such server implementation is likely to also want to
advertise other IMAP4rev1 extensions that were folded into IMAP4rev2;
see [Appendix E](#changesFromIMAP4rev1){.xref}.) While some IMAP4rev1
responses were removed in IMAP4rev2, their presence will not break
IMAP4rev2-only clients.[¶](#appendix-A-1){.pilcrow}

If both IMAP4rev1 and IMAP4rev2 are advertised, an IMAP client that
wants to use IMAP4rev2 [MUST]{.bcp14} issue an \"ENABLE IMAP4rev2\"
command.[¶](#appendix-A-2){.pilcrow}

When compared to IMAP4rev1, some request data items, corresponding
response data items, and responses were removed in IMAP4rev2. See
[Appendix E](#changesFromIMAP4rev1){.xref} for more details. With the
exception of obsolete SEARCH and RECENT responses, servers advertising
both IMAP4rev1 and IMAP4rev2 would never return such removed response
data items/responses unless explicitly requested by an IMAPrev1
client.[¶](#appendix-A-3){.pilcrow}

Servers advertising both IMAP4rev1 and IMAP4rev2 [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
generate UTF-8-quoted strings unless the client has issued \"ENABLE
IMAP4rev2\". Consider implementation of mechanisms described or
referenced in \[[IMAP-UTF-8](#RFC6855){.xref}\] to achieve this
goal.[¶](#appendix-A-4){.pilcrow}

Servers advertising both IMAP4rev1 and IMAP4rev2, and clients intending
to be compatible with IMAP4rev1 servers, [MUST]{.bcp14} be compatible
with the Mailbox International Naming Convention described in [Appendix
A.1](#mailbox-i18n){.xref}.[¶](#appendix-A-5){.pilcrow}

Also see [Appendix D](#body-part-64bit){.xref} for special
considerations for servers that support 63-bit body part / message sizes
and want to advertise support for both IMAP4rev1 and
IMAP4rev2.[¶](#appendix-A-6){.pilcrow}

::: {#mailbox-i18n}
::: {#appendix-A.1 .section}
### [A.1.](#appendix-A.1){.section-number .selfRef} [Mailbox International Naming Convention for Compatibility with IMAP4rev1](#name-mailbox-international-namin){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-mailbox-international-namin}

Support for the Mailbox International Naming Convention described in
this section is not required for IMAP4rev2-only clients and servers. It
is only used for backward compatibility with IMAP4rev1
implementations.[¶](#appendix-A.1-1){.pilcrow}

By convention, international mailbox names in IMAP4rev1 are specified
using a modified version of the UTF-7 encoding described in
\[[UTF-7](#RFC2152){.xref}\]. Modified UTF-7 may also be usable in
servers that implement an earlier version of this
protocol.[¶](#appendix-A.1-2){.pilcrow}

In modified UTF-7, printable US-ASCII characters, except for \"&\",
represent themselves; that is, characters with octet values 0x20-0x25
and 0x27-0x7e. The character \"&\" (0x26) is represented by the 2-octet
sequence \"&-\".[¶](#appendix-A.1-3){.pilcrow}

All other characters (octet values 0x00-0x1f and 0x7f-0xff) are
represented in modified base64, with a further modification from
\[[UTF-7](#RFC2152){.xref}\] that \",\" is used instead of \"/\".
Modified base64 [MUST NOT]{.bcp14} be used to represent any printing of
a US-ASCII character that can represent itself. Only characters inside
the modified base64 alphabet are permitted in modified base64
text.[¶](#appendix-A.1-4){.pilcrow}

\"&\" is used to shift to modified base64 and \"-\" to shift back to
US-ASCII. There is no implicit shift from base64 to US-ASCII, and null
shifts (\"-&\" while in base64; note that \"&-\" while in US-ASCII means
\"&\") are not permitted. However, all names start in US-ASCII and
[MUST]{.bcp14} end in US-ASCII; that is, a name that ends with a
non-ASCII ISO-10646 character [MUST]{.bcp14} end with a
\"-\".[¶](#appendix-A.1-5){.pilcrow}

The purpose of these modifications is to correct the following problems
with UTF-7:[¶](#appendix-A.1-6){.pilcrow}

1.  [UTF-7 uses the \"+\" character for shifting; this conflicts with
    the common use of \"+\" in mailbox names, in particular USENET
    newsgroup names.[¶](#appendix-A.1-7.1){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-A.1-7.1}
2.  [UTF-7\'s encoding is base64, which uses the \"/\" character; this
    conflicts with the use of \"/\" as a popular hierarchy
    delimiter.[¶](#appendix-A.1-7.2){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-A.1-7.2}
3.  [UTF-7 prohibits the unencoded usage of \"\\\"; this conflicts with
    the use of \"\\\" as a popular hierarchy
    delimiter.[¶](#appendix-A.1-7.3){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-A.1-7.3}
4.  [UTF-7 prohibits the unencoded usage of \"\~\"; this conflicts with
    the use of \"\~\" in some servers as a home directory
    indicator.[¶](#appendix-A.1-7.4){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-A.1-7.4}
5.  [UTF-7 permits multiple alternate forms to represent the same
    string; in particular, printable US-ASCII characters can be
    represented in encoded
    form.[¶](#appendix-A.1-7.5){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-A.1-7.5}

Although modified UTF-7 is a convention, it establishes certain
requirements on the server handling of any mailbox name with an embedded
\"&\" character. In particular, server implementations [MUST]{.bcp14}
preserve the exact form of the modified base64 portion of a modified
UTF-7 name and treat that text as case sensitive, even if names are
otherwise case insensitive or case folded.[¶](#appendix-A.1-8){.pilcrow}

Server implementations [SHOULD]{.bcp14} verify that any mailbox name
with an embedded \"&\" character, used as an argument to CREATE, is: in
the correctly modified UTF-7 syntax; has no superfluous shifts; and has
no encoding in modified base64 of any printing US-ASCII character that
can represent itself. However, client implementations [MUST NOT]{.bcp14}
depend upon the server doing this and [SHOULD NOT]{.bcp14} attempt to
create a mailbox name with an embedded \"&\" character unless it
complies with the modified UTF-7 syntax.[¶](#appendix-A.1-9){.pilcrow}

Server implementations that export a mail store that does not follow the
modified UTF-7 convention [MUST]{.bcp14} convert any mailbox name that
contains either non-ASCII characters or the \"&\" character to modified
UTF-7.[¶](#appendix-A.1-10){.pilcrow}

-   [For example, here is a mailbox name that mixes English, Chinese,
    and Japanese text:
    \~peter/mail/&U,BTFw-/&ZeVnLIqe-[¶](#appendix-A.1-11.1){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-A.1-11.1}
-   [For example, the string \"&Jjo!\" is not a valid mailbox name
    because it does not contain a shift to US-ASCII before the \"!\".
    The correct form is \"&Jjo-!\". The string \"&U,BTFw-&ZeVnLIqe-\" is
    not permitted because it contains a superfluous shift. The correct
    form is
    \"&U,BTF2XlZyyKng-\".[¶](#appendix-A.1-11.2){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-A.1-11.2}
:::
:::
:::
:::

::: {#BINARY-compat}
::: {#appendix-B .section}
## [Appendix B.](#appendix-B){.section-number .selfRef} [Backward Compatibility with BINARY Extension](#name-backward-compatibility-with-){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-backward-compatibility-with-}

IMAP4rev2 incorporates a subset of functionality provided by the BINARY
extension \[[RFC3516](#RFC3516){.xref}\]; in particular, it includes
additional FETCH items (BINARY, BINARY.PEEK, and BINARY.SIZE) but not
extensions to the APPEND command. IMAP4rev2 implementations that support
full \[[RFC3516](#RFC3516){.xref}\] functionality need to also advertise
the BINARY capability in the CAPABILITY response / response
code.[¶](#appendix-B-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#LIST-EXTENDED-compat}
::: {#appendix-C .section}
## [Appendix C.](#appendix-C){.section-number .selfRef} [Backward Compatibility with LIST-EXTENDED Extension](#name-backward-compatibility-with-l){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-backward-compatibility-with-l}

IMAP4rev2 incorporates most of the functionality provided by the
LIST-EXTENDED extension \[[RFC5258](#RFC5258){.xref}\]. In particular,
the syntax for multiple mailbox patterns is not supported in IMAP4rev2,
unless LIST-EXTENDED capability is also advertised in the CAPABILITY
response / response code.[¶](#appendix-C-1){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#body-part-64bit}
::: {#appendix-D .section}
## [Appendix D.](#appendix-D){.section-number .selfRef} [63-Bit Body Part and Message Sizes](#name-63-bit-body-part-and-messag){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-63-bit-body-part-and-messag}

IMAP4rev2 increases allowed body part and message sizes that servers can
support from 32 to 63 bits. Server implementations don\'t have to
support 63-bit-long body parts/message sizes; however, client
implementations have to expect them.[¶](#appendix-D-1){.pilcrow}

As IMAP4rev1 didn\'t support 63-bit-long body part / message sizes,
there is an interoperability issue exposed by 63-bit-capable
servers/mailboxes that are accessible by both IMAP4rev1 and IMAP4rev2
email clients. As IMAP4rev1 would be unable to retrieve the full content
of messages bigger than 4 Gb, such servers either need to replace
messages bigger that 4 Gb with messages under 4 Gb or hide them from
IMAP4rev1 clients. This document doesn\'t prescribe any implementation
strategy to address this issue.[¶](#appendix-D-2){.pilcrow}
:::
:::

::: {#changesFromIMAP4rev1}
::: {#appendix-E .section}
## [Appendix E.](#appendix-E){.section-number .selfRef} [Changes from RFC 3501 / IMAP4rev1](#name-changes-from-rfc-3501-imap4){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-changes-from-rfc-3501-imap4}

Below is the summary of changes since RFC
3501:[¶](#appendix-E-1){.pilcrow}

1.  [Support for 64-bit message and body part
    sizes.[¶](#appendix-E-2.1){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.1}
2.  [Folded in IMAP NAMESPACE \[[RFC2342](#RFC2342){.xref}\], UNSELECT
    \[[RFC3691](#RFC3691){.xref}\], UIDPLUS
    \[[RFC4315](#RFC4315){.xref}\], ESEARCH
    \[[RFC4731](#RFC4731){.xref}\], SEARCHRES
    \[[RFC5182](#RFC5182){.xref}\], ENABLE
    \[[RFC5161](#RFC5161){.xref}\], IDLE \[[RFC2177](#RFC2177){.xref}\],
    SASL-IR \[[RFC4959](#RFC4959){.xref}\], LIST-EXTENDED
    \[[RFC5258](#RFC5258){.xref}\], LIST-STATUS
    \[[RFC5819](#RFC5819){.xref}\], MOVE \[[RFC6851](#RFC6851){.xref}\],
    and LITERAL- extensions \[[RFC7888](#RFC7888){.xref}\]. Also folded
    in IMAP ABNF extensions \[[RFC4466](#RFC4466){.xref}\], response
    codes \[[RFC5530](#RFC5530){.xref}\], the FETCH side of the BINARY
    extension \[[RFC3516](#RFC3516){.xref}\], and the list of new
    mailbox attributes from SPECIAL-USE
    \[[RFC6154](#RFC6154){.xref}\].[¶](#appendix-E-2.2){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.2}
3.  [Added STATUS SIZE \[[RFC8438](#RFC8438){.xref}\] and STATUS
    DELETED.[¶](#appendix-E-2.3){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.3}
4.  [SEARCH command now requires to return the ESEARCH response (SEARCH
    response is now
    deprecated).[¶](#appendix-E-2.4){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.4}
5.  [Clarified which SEARCH keys have to use substring match and which
    don\'t.[¶](#appendix-E-2.5){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.5}
6.  [Clarified that the server should decode parameter value
    continuations as described in \[[RFC2231](#RFC2231){.xref}\]. This
    requirement was hidden in \[[RFC2231](#RFC2231){.xref}\]
    itself.[¶](#appendix-E-2.6){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.6}
7.  [Clarified that the COPYUID response code is returned for both MOVE
    and UID MOVE.[¶](#appendix-E-2.7){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.7}
8.  [Tightened requirements about COPY/MOVE commands not creating a
    target mailbox. Also required them to return the TRYCREATE response
    code, if the target mailbox doesn\'t exist and can be
    created.[¶](#appendix-E-2.8){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.8}
9.  [Added the CLOSED response code from \[[RFC7162](#RFC7162){.xref}\].
    SELECT/EXAMINE when a mailbox is already selected now requires a
    CLOSED response code to be
    returned.[¶](#appendix-E-2.9){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.9}
10. [SELECT/EXAMINE are now required to return an untagged LIST
    response.[¶](#appendix-E-2.10){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.10}
11. [UNSEEN response code on SELECT/EXAMINE is now
    deprecated.[¶](#appendix-E-2.11){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.11}
12. [RECENT response on SELECT/EXAMINE, \\Recent flag, RECENT STATUS,
    and SEARCH NEW items are now
    deprecated.[¶](#appendix-E-2.12){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.12}
13. [Clarified that the server doesn\'t need to send a new
    PERMANENTFLAGS response code when a new keyword was successfully
    added and the server advertised \\\* earlier for the same
    mailbox.[¶](#appendix-E-2.13){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.13}
14. [For future extensibility, extended ABNF for tagged-ext-simple to
    allow for bare
    number64.[¶](#appendix-E-2.14){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.14}
15. [Added [SHOULD]{.bcp14} level requirement on IMAP servers to support
    \$MDNSent, \$Forwarded, \$Junk, \$NonJunk, and \$Phishing
    keywords.[¶](#appendix-E-2.15){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.15}
16. [Mailbox names and message headers now allow for UTF-8. Support for
    modified UTF-7 in mailbox names is not required, unless
    compatibility with IMAP4rev1 is
    desired.[¶](#appendix-E-2.16){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.16}
17. [Removed the CHECK command. Clients should use NOOP
    instead.[¶](#appendix-E-2.17){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.17}
18. [RFC822, RFC822.HEADER, and RFC822.TEXT FETCH data items were
    deprecated. Clients should use the corresponding BODY\[\] variants
    instead.[¶](#appendix-E-2.18){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.18}
19. [LSUB command was deprecated. Clients should use LIST (SUBSCRIBED)
    instead.[¶](#appendix-E-2.19){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.19}
20. [IDLE command can now return updates not related to the currently
    selected mailbox
    state.[¶](#appendix-E-2.20){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.20}
21. [All unsolicited FETCH updates are required to include
    UID.[¶](#appendix-E-2.21){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.21}
22. [Clarified that client implementations [MUST]{.bcp14} ignore
    response codes that they do not recognize. (Changed from a
    [SHOULD]{.bcp14} to a
    [MUST]{.bcp14}.)[¶](#appendix-E-2.22){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.22}
23. [resp-text ABNF non-terminal was updated to allow for empty
    text.[¶](#appendix-E-2.23){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.23}
24. [After ENABLE, IMAP4rev2 human-readable response text can include
    non-ASCII encoded in
    UTF-8.[¶](#appendix-E-2.24){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.24}
25. [Updated to use modern TLS-related recommendations as per
    \[[RFC7525](#RFC7525){.xref}\], \[[RFC7817](#RFC7817){.xref}\], and
    \[[RFC8314](#RFC8314){.xref}\].[¶](#appendix-E-2.25){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.25}
26. [Added warnings about use of ALERT response codes and PREAUTH
    response.[¶](#appendix-E-2.26){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.26}
27. [Replaced DIGEST-MD5 SASL mechanism with SCRAM-SHA-256. DIGEST-MD5
    was deprecated.[¶](#appendix-E-2.27){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.27}
28. [Clarified that any command received from the client resets server
    autologout timer.[¶](#appendix-E-2.28){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.28}
29. [Revised IANA registration procedure for IMAP extensions and removed
    \"X\" convention in accordance with
    \[[BCP178](#BCP178){.xref}\].[¶](#appendix-E-2.29){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.29}
30. [Loosened requirements on servers when closing connections to be
    more aligned with existing
    practices.[¶](#appendix-E-2.30){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-E-2.30}
:::
:::

::: {#recommended-extensions}
::: {#appendix-F .section}
## [Appendix F.](#appendix-F){.section-number .selfRef} [Other Recommended IMAP Extensions](#name-other-recommended-imap-exte){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-other-recommended-imap-exte}

Support for the following extensions is recommended for all IMAP clients
and servers. While they significantly reduce bandwidth and/or number of
round trips used by IMAP in certain situations, the EXTRA WG decided
that requiring them as a part of IMAP4rev2 would push the bar to
implement too high for new implementations. Also note that the absence
of any IMAP extension from this list doesn\'t make it somehow deficient
or not recommended for use with IMAP4rev2.[¶](#appendix-F-1){.pilcrow}

1.  [Quick Mailbox Resynchronization (QRESYNC) and CONDSTORE extensions
    \[[RFC7162](#RFC7162){.xref}\]. They make discovering changes to
    IMAP mailboxes more efficient, at the expense of storing a bit more
    state.[¶](#appendix-F-2.1){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-F-2.1}
2.  [OBJECTID extension \[[RFC8474](#RFC8474){.xref}\] helps with
    preserving the IMAP client cache when messages are moved/copied or
    mailboxes are
    renamed.[¶](#appendix-F-2.2){.pilcrow}]{#appendix-F-2.2}
:::
:::

## [Acknowledgements](#name-acknowledgements){.section-name .selfRef} {#name-acknowledgements}

Earlier draft versions of this document were edited by [Mark
Crispin]{.contact-name}. Sadly, he is no longer available to help with
this work. Editors of this revision are hoping that Mark would have
approved.[¶](#appendix-G-1){.pilcrow}

[Chris Newman]{.contact-name} has contributed text on I18N and use of
UTF-8 in messages and mailbox names.[¶](#appendix-G-2){.pilcrow}

Thank you to [Tony Hansen]{.contact-name} for helping with the index
generation. Thank you to [Murray Kucherawy]{.contact-name}, [Timo
Sirainen]{.contact-name}, [Bron Gondwana]{.contact-name}, [Stephan
Bosch]{.contact-name}, [Robert Sparks]{.contact-name}, [Arnt
Gulbrandsen]{.contact-name}, [Benjamin Kaduk]{.contact-name}, [Daniel
Migaul]{.contact-name}, [Roman Danyliw]{.contact-name}, and [Éric
Vyncke]{.contact-name} for extensive
feedback.[¶](#appendix-G-3){.pilcrow}

This document incorporates text from \[[RFC2342](#RFC2342){.xref}\] (by
[Mike Gahrns]{.contact-name} and [Chris Newman]{.contact-name}),
\[[RFC3516](#RFC3516){.xref}\] (by [Lyndon Nerenberg]{.contact-name}),
\[[RFC4315](#RFC4315){.xref}\] (by [Mark Crispin]{.contact-name}),
\[[RFC4466](#RFC4466){.xref}\] (by [Cyrus Daboo]{.contact-name}),
\[[RFC4731](#RFC4731){.xref}\] (by [Dave Cridland]{.contact-name}),
\[[RFC4959](#RFC4959){.xref}\] (by [Rob Siemborski]{.contact-name} and
[Arnt Gulbrandsen]{.contact-name}), \[[RFC5161](#RFC5161){.xref}\] (by
[Arnt Gulbrandsen]{.contact-name}), \[[RFC5465](#RFC5465){.xref}\] (by
[Arnt Gulbrandsen]{.contact-name} and [Curtis King]{.contact-name}),
\[[RFC5530](#RFC5530){.xref}\] (by [Arnt Gulbrandsen]{.contact-name}),
\[[RFC5819](#RFC5819){.xref}\] (by [Timo Sirainen]{.contact-name}),
\[[RFC6154](#RFC6154){.xref}\] (by [Jamie Nicolson]{.contact-name}),

[Ned Freed]{.contact-name}), and \[[RFC8438](#RFC8438){.xref}\] (by
[Stephan Bosch]{.contact-name}), so work done by authors/editors of
these documents is appreciated. Note that editors of this document were
redacted from the above list.[¶](#appendix-G-4){.pilcrow}

The CHILDREN return option was originally proposed by [Mike
Gahrns]{.contact-name} and [Raymond Cheng]{.contact-name} in
\[[RFC3348](#RFC3348){.xref}\]. Most of the information in [Section
6.3.9.5](#children){.xref} is taken directly from their original
specification
\[[RFC3348](#RFC3348){.xref}\].[¶](#appendix-G-5){.pilcrow}

Thank you to [Damian Poddebniak]{.contact-name}, [Fabian
Ising]{.contact-name}, [Hanno Boeck]{.contact-name}, and [Sebastian
Schinzel]{.contact-name} for pointing out that the ENABLE command should
be a member of \"command-auth\" and not \"command-any\" ABNF production,
as well as pointing out security issues associated with ALERT, PREAUTH,
and other responses received before
authentication.[¶](#appendix-G-6){.pilcrow}
